And while she be wait there , think such lovely thought , a neighbour 's boy come run up -- a boy who do n't know about her romance -- and cry out that Malcolm Ward have be kill by his gun go off accidentally .
Emily just put her hand to her heart -- so -- and fell , all white and broken among the fern .
And when she come back to life she never cry or lament .
She be CHANGED .
She be never , never like herself again ; and she be never content unless she be dress in her blue muslin and wait under the birch .
She get paler and paler every day , but the pink butterfly grow red , until it look just like a stain of blood on her white cheek .
When the winter come she die .
But next spring '' -- the Story Girl drop her voice to a whisper that be a audible and thrill a her louder tone -- `` people begin to tell that Emily be sometimes see wait under the birch still .
Nobody know just who tell it first .
But more than one person saw her .
Grandfather saw her when he be a little boy .
And my mother saw her once . ''
`` Did YOU ever see her ? ''
ask Felix skeptically .
`` No , but I shall some day , if I keep on believing in her , '' say the Story Girl confidently .
`` I would n't like to see her .
I 'd be afraid , '' say Cecily with a shiver .
`` There would n't be anything to be afraid of , '' say the Story Girl reassuringly .
`` It 's not a if it be a strange ghost .
It 's our own family ghost , so of course it would n't hurt u . ''
We be not so sure of this .
Ghosts be unchancy folk , even if they be our family ghost .
The Story Girl have make the tale very real to u .
We be glad we have not hear it in the evening .
How could we ever have get back to the house through the shadow and sway branch of a darken orchard ?
As it be , we be almost afraid to look up it , lest we should see the waiting , blue-clad Emily under Uncle Alec 's tree .
But all we saw be Felicity , tear over the green sward , her curl streaming behind her in a golden cloud .
`` Felicity 's afraid she 's missed something , '' remark the Story Girl in a tone of quiet amusement .
`` Is your breakfast ready , Felicity , or have I time to tell the boy the Story of the Poet Who Was Kissed ? ''
`` Breakfast be ready , but we ca n't have it till father be through attend to the sick cow , so you will likely have time , '' answer Felicity .
Felix and I could n't keep our eye off her .
Crimson-cheeked , shining-eyed from her haste , her face be like a rise of youth .
But when the Story Girl speak , we forget to look at Felicity .
`` About ten year after Grandfather and Grandmother King be marry , a young man come to visit them .
He be a distant relative of grandmother 's and he be a Poet .
He be just begin to be famous .
He be VERY famous afterward .
He come into the orchard to write a poem , and he fell asleep with his head on a bench that use to be under grandfather 's tree .
Then Great-Aunt Edith come into the orchard .
She be not a Great-Aunt then , of course .
She be only eighteen , with red lip and black , black hair and eye .
They say she be always full of mischief .
She have be away and have just come home , and she do n't know about the Poet .
But when she saw him , sleep there , she think he be a cousin they have be expect from Scotland .
And she tiptoe up -- so -- and bent over -- so -- and kiss his cheek .
Then he open his big blue eye and look up into Edith 's face .
She blush as red a a rise , for she know she have do a dreadful thing .
This could not be her cousin from Scotland .
She know , for he have write so to her , that he have eye as black a her own .
Edith run away and hid ; and of course she felt still bad when she find out that he be a famous poet .

We have SEEN it all -- the sleeping genius -- the roguish , red-lipped girl -- the kiss drop as lightly a a rose-petal on the sunburned cheek .

`` Well , in a book they would have , but you see this be in real life , '' say the Story Girl .

I like it when Peter play the poet .
I do n't like it when Dan be the poet because he be so freckled and screw his eye up so tight .
But you can hardly ever coax Peter to be the poet -- except when Felicity be Edith -- and Dan be so obliging that way . ''
`` What be Peter like ? ''
I ask .
`` Peter be splendid .
His mother live on the Markdale road and wash for a living .

He have never come back , and they do n't know whether he be alive or dead .
Is n't that a nice way to behave to your family ?
Peter have work for his board ever since he be six .
Uncle Roger send him to school , and pay him wage in summer .

`` I like Peter well enough in his place , '' say Felicity primly , `` but you make far too much of him , mother say .
He be only a hired boy , and he have n't be well bring up , and have n't much education .
I do n't think you should make such an equal of him a you do . ''
Laughter ripple over the Story Girl 's face a shadow wave go over ripe wheat before a wind .
`` Peter be a real gentleman , and he be more interesting than YOU could ever be , if you be bring up and educate for a hundred year , '' she say .
`` He can hardly write , '' say Felicity .
`` William the Conqueror could n't write at all , '' say the Story Girl crushingly .
`` He never go to church , and he never say his prayer , '' retort Felicity , uncrushed .
`` I do , too , '' say Peter himself , suddenly appear through a little gap in the hedge .
`` I say my prayer sometimes . ''
This Peter be a slim , shapely fellow , with laughing black eye and thick black curl .
Early in the season a it be , he be barefooted .
His attire consist of a faded , gingham shirt and a scanty pair of corduroy knickerbockers ; but he wear it with such an unconscious air of purple and fine linen that he seem to be much good dress than he really be .
`` You do n't pray very often , '' insist Felicity .
`` Well , God will be all the more likely to listen to me if I do n't pester Him all the time , '' argue Peter .
This be rank heresy to Felicity , but the Story Girl look a if she think there might be something in it .
`` You NEVER go to church , anyhow , '' continue Felicity , determine not to be argue down .
`` Well , I ai n't go to church till I 've make up my mind whether I 'm go to be a Methodist or a Presbyterian .
Aunt Jane be a Methodist .
My mother ai n't much of anything but I mean to be something .
It 's more respectable to be a Methodist or a Presbyterian , or SOMETHING , than not to be anything .
When I 've settle what I 'm to be I 'm go to church same a you . ''
`` That 's not the same a be BORN something , '' say Felicity loftily .
`` I think it 's a good deal well to pick your own religion than have to take it just because it be what your folk have , '' retort Peter .
`` Now , never mind quarrelling , '' say Cecily .
`` You leave Peter alone , Felicity .
Peter , this be Beverley King , and this be Felix .
And we 're all go to be good friend and have a lovely summer together .
Think of the game we can have !
But if you go squabble you 'll spoil it all .
Peter , what be you go to do to-day ? ''
`` Harrow the wood field and dig your Aunt Olivia 's flower bed . ''
`` Aunt Olivia and I plant sweet pea yesterday , '' say the Story Girl , `` and I plant a little bed of my own .
I be NOT go to dig them up this year to see if they have sprout .
It be bad for them .
I shall try to cultivate patience , no matter how long they be come up . ''
`` I be go to help mother plant the vegetable garden to-day , '' say Felicity .
`` Oh , I never like the vegetable garden , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Except when I be hungry .
Then I DO like to go and look at the nice little row of onion and beet .
But I love a flower garden .
I think I could be always good if I live in a garden all the time . ''
`` Adam and Eve live in a garden all the time , '' say Felicity , `` and THEY be far from be always good . ''
`` They might n't have keep good as long a they do if they have n't live in a garden , '' say the Story Girl .
We be now summon to breakfast .
Peter and the Story Girl slip away through the gap , follow by Paddy , and the rest of u walk up the orchard to the house .
`` Well , what do you think of the Story Girl ? ''
ask Felicity .
`` She 's just fine , '' say Felix , enthusiastically .
`` I never hear anything like her to tell story . ''
`` She ca n't cook , '' say Felicity , `` and she have n't a good complexion .
Mind you , she say she 's go to be an actress when she grow up .
Is n't that dreadful ? ''
We do n't exactly see why .
`` Oh , because actress be always wicked people , '' say Felicity in a shocked tone .
`` But I daresay the Story Girl will go and be one just as soon a she can .
Her father will back her up in it .
He be an artist , you know . ''
Evidently Felicity think artist and actress and all such poor trash be member one of another .
`` Aunt Olivia say the Story Girl be fascinate , '' say Cecily .
The very adjective !
Felix and I recognize it beautiful fitness at once .
Yes , the Story Girl WAS fascinate and that be the final word to be say on the subject .
Dan do not come down until breakfast be half over , and Aunt Janet talk to him after a fashion which make u realize that it would be well to keep , a the piquant country phrase go , from the rough side of her tongue .
But all thing consider , we like the prospect of our summer very much .
Felicity to look at -- the Story Girl to tell u tale of wonder -- Cecily to admire u -- Dan and Peter to play with -- what more could reasonable fellow want ?
CHAPTER IV .
THE WEDDING VEIL OF THE PROUD PRINCESS When we have live for a fortnight in Carlisle we belong there , and the freedom of all it small fry be confer on u .
With Peter and Dan , with Felicity and Cecily and the Story Girl , with pale , gray-eyed little Sara Ray , we be boon companion .
We go to school , of course ; and certain home chore be assign to each of u for the faithful performance of which we be hold responsible .
But we have long hour for play .
Even Peter have plenty of spare time when the planting be over .
We get along very well with each other in the main , in spite of some minor difference of opinion .
As for the grown-up denizen of our small world , they suit u also .
We adore Aunt Olivia ; she be pretty and merry and kind ; and , above all , she have master to perfection the rare art of let child alone .
If we keep ourselves tolerably clean , and refrain from quarrel or talk slang , Aunt Olivia do not worry u .
Aunt Janet , on the contrary , give u so much good advice and be so constantly tell u to do this or not to do the other thing , that we could not remember half her instruction , and do not try .
Uncle Roger be , a we have be inform , quite jolly and fond of teasing .
We like him ; but we have an uncomfortable feeling that the meaning of his remark be not always that which meet the ear .
Sometimes we believe Uncle Roger be make fun of u , and the deadly seriousness of youth in u resent that .
The Uncle Alec we give our warm love .
We felt that we always have a friend at court in Uncle Alec , no matter what we do or leave undone .
And we never have to turn HIS speech inside out to discover their meaning .
The social life of juvenile Carlisle centre in the day and Sunday Schools .
We be especially interested in our Sunday School , for we be fortunate enough to be assign to a teacher who make our lesson so interesting that we no longer regard Sunday School attendance a a disagreeable weekly duty ; but instead look forward to it with pleasure , and try to carry out our teacher 's gentle precept -- at least on Mondays and Tuesdays .
I be afraid the remembrance grow a little dim the rest of the week .
She be also deeply interested in mission ; and one talk on this subject inspire the Story Girl to do a little home missionary work on her own account .
The only thing she could think of , along this line , be to persuade Peter to go to church .
Felicity do not approve of the design , and say so plainly .
`` He wo n't know how to behave , for he 's never be inside a church door in his life , '' she warn the Story Girl .
`` He 'll likely do something awful , and then you 'll feel ashamed and wish you 'd never ask him to go , and we 'll all be disgrace .
It 's all right to have our mite box for the heathen , and send missionary to them .
They 're far away and we do n't have to associate with them .
But I do n't want to have to sit in a pew with a hired boy . ''
But the Story Girl undauntedly continue to coax the reluctant Peter .
It be not an easy matter .
Peter do not come of a churchgoing stock ; and besides , he allege , he have not yet make up his mind whether to be a Presbyterian or a Methodist .
`` It be n't a bit of difference which you be , '' plead the Story Girl .
`` They both go to heaven . ''
`` But one way must be easy or good than the other , or else they 'd all be one kind , '' argue Peter .
`` I want to find the easy way .
And I 've get a hankering after the Methodists .
My Aunt Jane be a Methodist . ''
`` Is n't she one still ? ''
ask Felicity pertly .
`` Well , I do n't know exactly .
She 's dead , '' say Peter rebukingly .
`` Do people go on be just the same after they 're dead ? ''
`` No , of course not .
They 're angel then -- not Methodists or anything , but just angel .
That be , if they go to heaven . ''
`` S'posen they go to the other place ? ''
But Felicity 's theology break down at this point .
She turn her back on Peter and walk disdainfully away .
The Story Girl return to the main point with a new argument .
`` We have such a lovely minister , Peter .
He look just like the picture of St. John my father send me , only he be old and his hair be white .
I know you 'd like him .
And even if you be go to be a Methodist it wo n't hurt you to go to the Presbyterian church .
The near Methodist church be six mile away , at Markdale , and you ca n't attend there just now .
Go to the Presbyterian church until you 're old enough to have a horse . ''
`` But s ` posen I get too fond of be Presbyterian and could n't change if I want to ? ''
object Peter .
Altogether , the Story Girl have a hard time of it ; but she persevere ; and one day she come to u with the announcement that Peter have yield .
`` He 's go to church with u to-morrow , '' she say triumphantly .
We be out in Uncle Roger 's hill pasture , sit on some smooth , round stone under a clump of birch .
Behind u be an old gray fence , with violet and dandelion thick in it corner .
Below u be the Carlisle valley , with it orchard-embowered homestead , and fertile meadow .
Its upper end be dim with a delicate spring mist .
Winds blow up the field like wave upon wave of sweet savour -- spice of bracken and balsam .
We be eat little jam `` turnover , '' which Felicity have make for u .
Felicity 's turnover be perfection .
I look at her and wonder why it be not enough that she should be so pretty and capable of make such turnover .
If she be only more interesting !
Felicity have not a particle of the nameless charm and allurement which hung about every motion of the Story Girl , and make itself manifest in her light word and most careless glance .
Ah well , one can not have every good gift !
The Story Girl have no dimple at her slim , brown wrist .
We all enjoy our turnover except Sara Ray .
She eat hers but she know she should not have do so .
Her mother do not approve of snack between meal , or of jam turnover at any time .
Once , when Sara be in a brown study , I ask her what she be think of .
`` I 'm try to think of something ma have n't forbid , '' she answer with a sigh .
We be all glad to hear that Peter be go to church , except Felicity .
She be full of gloomy foreboding and warning .
`` I 'm surprised at you , Felicity King , '' say Cecily severely .
`` You ought to be glad that poor boy be go to get start in the right way . ''
`` There 's a great big patch on his best pair of trouser , '' protest Felicity .
`` Well , that 's good than a hole , '' say the Story Girl , address herself daintily to her turnover .
`` God wo n't notice the patch . ''
`` No , but the Carlisle people will , '' retort Felicity , in a tone which imply that what the Carlisle people think be far more important .
`` And I do n't believe that Peter have get a decent stocking to his name .
What will you feel like if he go to church with the skin of his legs showing through the hole , Miss Story Girl ? ''
`` I 'm not a bit afraid , '' say the Story Girl staunchly .
`` Peter know good than that . ''
`` Well , all I hope be that he 'll wash behind his ear , '' say Felicity resignedly .
`` How be Pat to-day ? ''
ask Cecily , by way of change the conversation .
`` Pat be n't a bit well .
He just mop about the kitchen , '' say the Story Girl anxiously .
`` I go out to the barn and I saw a mouse .
I have a stick in my hand and I fetch a swipe at it -- so .
I kill it stone dead .
Then I take it in to Paddy .
Will you believe it ?
He would n't even look at it .
I 'm so worried .

whisper Cecily .

`` I 'd be awful sorry myself if Pat die .
But if he DID , we 'd have to give him the right kind of a funeral , '' he protest .
`` Why , Paddy just seem like one of the family . ''
The Story Girl finish her turnover , and stretch herself out on the grass , pillow her chin in her hand and look at the sky .
She be bare head , a usual , and her scarlet ribbon be bind filletwise about her head .

`` A wedding veil , '' say Cecily .
`` That be just what it be -- the Wedding Veil of the Proud Princess .
I know a story about it .
I read it in a book .
Once upon a time '' -- the Story Girl 's eye grow dreamy , and her accent float away on the summer air like wind-blown rise petal -- `` there be a princess who be the most beautiful princess in the world , and king from all land come to woo her for a bride .
But she be as proud a she be beautiful .
She laugh all her suitor to scorn .
And when her father urge her to choose one of them a her husband she draw herself up haughtily -- so -- '' The Story Girl sprang to her foot and for a moment we saw the proud princess of the old tale in all her scornful loveliness -- `` and she say , '' ' I will not wed until a king come who can conquer all king .
Then I shall be the wife of the king of the world and no one can hold herself high than I. ' `` So every king go to war to prove that he could conquer every one else , and there be a great deal of bloodshed and misery .
But the proud princess laugh and sang , and she and her maiden work at a wonderful lace veil which she mean to wear when the king of all king come .
It be a very beautiful veil ; but her maiden whisper that a man have die and a woman 's heart have break for every stitch set in it .
`` Just when a king thought he have conquer everybody some other king would come and conquer HIM ; and so it go on until it do not seem likely the proud princess would ever get a husband at all .
But still her pride be so great that she would not yield , even though everybody except the king who want to marry her , hat her for the suffering she have cause .
One day a horn be blow at the palace gate ; and there be one tall man in complete armor with his visor down , rid on a white horse .
When he say he have come to marry the princess every one laugh , for he have no retinue and no beautiful apparel , and no golden crown . ''
` But I be the king who conquer all king , ' he say . ''
` You must prove it before I shall marry you , ' say the proud princess .
But she tremble and turn pale , for there be something in his voice that frighten her .
And when he laugh , his laughter be still more dreadful . '' '
I can easily prove it , beautiful princess , ' he say , ` but you must go with me to my kingdom for the proof .
Marry me now , and you and I and your father and all your court will ride straightway to my kingdom ; and if you be not satisfied then that I be the king who conquer all king you may give me back my ring and return home free of me forever more . '
`` It be a strange wooing and the friend of the princess beg her to refuse .
But her pride whisper that it would be such a wonderful thing to be the queen of the king of the world ; so she consent ; and her maiden dress her , and put on the long lace veil that have be so many year a-making .
Then they be marry at once , but the bridegroom never lift his visor and no one saw his face .
The proud princess hold herself more proudly than ever , but she be as white a her veil .
And there be no laughter or merry-making , such a should be at a wedding , and every one look at every one else with fear in his eye .
`` After the wed the bridegroom lift his bride before him on his white horse , and her father and all the member of his court mount , too , and rode after them .
On and on they ride , and the sky grow darker and the wind blew and wail , and the shade of even come down .
And just in the twilight they ride into a dark valley , fill with tomb and graf . ''
` Why have you bring me here ? '
cry the proud princess angrily . ''
` This be my kingdom , ' he answer .
` These be the tomb of the king I have conquer .
Behold me , beautiful princess .
I be Death ! '
`` He lift his visor .
All saw his awful face .
The proud princess shriek . ''
` Come to my arm , my bride , ' he cry . '
I have win you fairly .
I be the king who conquer all king ! '
`` He clasp her faint form to his breast and spur his white horse to the tomb .
A tempest of rain break over the valley and blot them from sight .
Very sadly the old king and courtier ride home , and never , never again do human eye behold the proud princess .
But when those long , white cloud sweep across the sky , the country people in the land where she live say , ` Look you , there be the Wedding Veil of the Proud Princess . ' ''
The weird spell of the tale rest on u for some moment after the Story Girl have finish .
We have walk with her in the place of death and grown cold with the horror that chill the heart of the poor princess .
Dan presently break the spell .
`` You see it do n't do to be too proud , Felicity , '' he remark , give her a poke .
`` You 'd better not say too much about Peter 's patch . ''
CHAPTER V. PETER GOES TO CHURCH There be no Sunday School the next afternoon , a superintendent and teacher wish to attend a communion service at Markdale .
The Carlisle service be in the evening , and at sunset we be wait at Uncle Alec 's front door for Peter and the Story Girl .
None of the grown-ups be go to church .
Aunt Olivia have a sick headache and Uncle Roger stay home with her .
Aunt Janet and Uncle Alec have go to the Markdale service and have not yet return .
Felicity and Cecily be wear their new summer muslin for the first time -- and be acutely conscious of the fact .

Presently Peter and the Story Girl appear , and we be all more or less relieve to see that Peter look quite respectable , despite the indisputable patch on his trouser .
His face be rosy , his thick black curl be smoothly comb , and his tie be neatly bow ; but it be his legs which we scrutinize most anxiously .
At first glance they seem well enough ; but close inspection reveal something not altogether customary .
`` What be the matter with your stocking , Peter ? ''
ask Dan bluntly .
`` Oh , I have n't a pair without hole in the leg , '' answer Peter easily , `` because ma have n't time to darn them this week .
So I put on two pair .
The hole do n't come in the same place , and you 'd never notice them unless you look right close . ''
`` Have you get a cent for collection ? ''
demand Felicity .
`` I 've get a Yankee cent .
I s ` pose it will do , wo n't it ? ''

`` Oh , no , no .

`` I have n't another cent .
I only get fifty cent a week and I give it all to ma last night . ''
But Peter must have a cent .
Felicity would have give him one herself -- and she be none too lavish of her copper -- rather than have him go without one .

The Carlisle church be a very old-fashioned one , with a square , ivy-hung tower .
It be shade by tall elm , and the graveyard surround it completely , many of the graf be directly under it window .
We always take the corner path through it , pass the King plot where our kindred of four generation sleep in a green solitude of waver light and shadow .
There be Great-grandfather King 's flat tombstone of rough Island sandstone , so overgrown with ivy that we could hardly read it lengthy inscription , record his whole history in brief , and finish with eight line of original verse compose by his widow .
I do not think that poetry be Great-grandmother King 's strong point .
When Felix read it , on our first Sunday in Carlisle , he remark dubiously that it LOOKED like poetry but do n't SOUND like it .

The Story Girl linger to lay a bunch of wild violet , misty blue and faintly sweet , on her mother 's grave ; and then she read aloud the verse on the stone . ''
` They be lovely and pleasant in their life and in their death they be not divide . ' ''
The tone of her voice bring out the poignant and immortal beauty and pathos of that wonderful old lament .
The girl wipe their eye ; and we boys felt a if we might have do so , too , have nobody be look .
What good epitaph could any one wish than to have it say that he be lovely and pleasant in his life ?
When I hear the Story Girl read it I make a secret compact with myself that I would try to deserve such an epitaph .
`` I wish I have a family plot , '' say Peter , rather wistfully .

The interior of the church be as old-fashioned a it exterior .

It 's nice . ''

We know Elder Frewen quite well and like him ; he be Aunt Janet 's cousin and often visit her .

Peter sidle up to her .

It be this way -- '' `` Do n't you ever speak to me again , '' say the Story Girl , in a tone of cold concentrate fury .

he whisper .

`` Well , I do n't mean to .

This pulpit door be make for speerits ' -- and I want to laugh .
And then Mr. Frewen come -- and I think of her story about his sidewhiskers -- how when his first wife die of information of the lung he go court Celia Ward , and Celia tell him she would n't marry him unless he shave them whisker off .
And he would n't , just to be stubborn .
And one day one of them catch fire , when he be burn brush , and burn off , and every one thought he 'd HAVE to shave the other off then .
But he do n't and just go round with one whisker till the burned one grow out .

I just remember that story , and I think I could see him , take up the cent so solemn , with one long whisker ; and the laugh just laugh itself before I could help it . ''
We all explode with laughter on the spot , much to the horror of Mrs. Abraham Ward , who be just drive past , and who come up the next day and tell Aunt Janet we have `` act scandalous '' on the road home from church .
We felt ashamed ourselves , because we know people should conduct themselves decently and in order on Sunday farings-forth .

Even Felicity laugh .

`` I 'm go to keep on go to church , '' Peter tell her .

I s ` pose I might ask the minister about it . ''

`` Why not ?
What be minister for if they ai n't to tell people how to get to heaven ? ''
`` Oh , well , it 's all right for grown-ups to ask them thing , of course .
But it be n't respectful for little boy -- especially hired boy . ''
`` I do n't see why .

`` What do God look like ? ''
he say .
It appear that none of u have any idea .

Ah , do we ever `` feel quite the same '' towards people who destroy our illusion ?
Shall I ever be able to forgive the brutal creature who first tell me there be no such person a Santa Claus ?
He be a boy , three year old than myself ; and he may now , for aught I know , be a most useful and respectable member of society , beloved by his kind .

We wait at Uncle Alec 's door for the others to come up .

No , sir !
And I 'm go to church and Sunday School regular , and I 'll say my prayer every night .

And look here !
I 've think of the way my Aunt Jane use to give medicine to a cat .

They go away together hand in hand , children-wise , up the lane of spruce cross with bar of moonlight .
And there be peace over all that fresh and flowery land , and peace in our little heart .
CHAPTER VI .
THE MYSTERY OF GOLDEN MILESTONE Paddy be smear with medicated lard the next day , all of u assist at the rite , although the Story Girl be high priestess .
Then , out of regard for mat and cushion , he be keep in durance vile in the granary until he have lick his fur clean .
This treatment be repeat every day for a week , Pat recover his usual health and spirit , and our mind be set at rest to enjoy the next excitement -- collect for a school library fund .
Our teacher think it would be an excellent thing to have a library in connection with the school ; and he suggest that each of the pupil should try to see how much money he or she could raise for the project during the month of June .
We might earn it by honest toil , or gather it in by contribution levy on our friend .
The result be a determined rivalry a to which pupil should collect the large sum ; and this rivalry be especially intense in our home coterie .
Our relative start u with a quarter apiece .
For the rest , we know we must depend on our own exertion .
Peter be handicap at the beginning by the fact that he have no family friend to finance him .
`` If my Aunt Jane 'd be live she 'd have give me something , '' he remark .
`` And if my father have n't run away he might have give me something too .
But I 'm go to do the best I can anyhow .
Your Aunt Olivia say I can have the job of gather the egg , and I 'm to have one egg out of every dozen to sell for myself . ''
Felicity make a similar bargain with her mother .
The Story Girl and Cecily be each to be pay ten cent a week for wash dish in their respective home .
Felix and Dan contract to keep the garden free from weed .
I catch brook trout in the westering valley of spruce and sell them for a cent apiece .
Sara Ray be the only unhappy one among u .
She could do nothing .
She have no relative in Carlisle except her mother , and her mother do not approve of the school library project , and would not give Sara a cent , or put her in any way of earn one .
To Sara , this be humiliation indescribable .
She felt herself an outcast and an alien to our busy little circle , where each member count every day , with miserly delight , his slowly increase hoard of small cash .
`` I 'm just go to pray to God to send me some money , '' she announce desperately at last .
`` I do n't believe that will do any good , '' say Dan .
`` He give lot of thing , but he do n't give money , because people can earn that for themselves . ''
`` I ca n't , '' say Sara , with passionate defiance .
`` I think He ought to take that into account . ''
`` Do n't worry , dear , '' say Cecily , who always pour balm .
`` If you ca n't collect any money everybody will know it be n't your fault . ''
`` I wo n't ever feel like read a single book in the library if I ca n't give something to it , '' mourn Sara .
Dan and the girl and I be sit in a row on Aunt Olivia 's garden fence , watch Felix weed .
Felix work well , although he do not like weed -- `` fat boy never do , '' Felicity inform him .
Felix pretend not to hear her , but I know he do , because his ear grow red .
Felix 's face never blush , but his ear always give him away .
As for Felicity , she do not say thing like that out of malice prepense .
It never occur to her that Felix do not like to be call fat .
`` I always feel so sorry for the poor weed , '' say the Story Girl dreamily .
`` It must be very hard to be root up . ''
`` They should n't grow in the wrong place , '' say Felicity mercilessly .
`` When weed go to heaven I suppose they will be flower , '' continue the Story Girl .
`` You do think such queer thing , '' say Felicity .
`` A rich man in Toronto have a floral clock in his garden , '' I say .
`` It look just like the face of a clock , and there be flower in it that open at every hour , so that you can always tell the time . ''
`` Oh , I wish we have one here , '' exclaim Cecily .
`` What would be the use of it ? ''
ask the Story Girl a little disdainfully .
`` Nobody ever want to know the time in a garden . ''
I slip away at this point , suddenly remember that it be time to take a dose of magic seed .
I have buy it from Billy Robinson three day before in school .
Billy have assure me that it would make me grow fast .
I be begin to feel secretly worry because I do not grow .
I have overhear Aunt Janet say I be go to be short , like Uncle Alec .
Now , I love Uncle Alec , but I want to be tall than he be .
So when Billy confide to me , under solemn promise of secrecy , that he have some `` magic seed , '' which would make boy grow , and would sell me a box of it for ten cent , I jump at the offer .
Billy be taller than any boy of his age in Carlisle , and he assure me it all come from take magic seed .
`` I be a regular runt before I begin , '' he say , `` and look at me now .
I get it from Peg Bowen .
She 's a witch , you know .
I would n't go near her again for a bushel of magic seed .
It be an awful experience .
I have n't much leave , but I guess I 've enough to do me till I 'm as tall a I want to be .
You must take a pinch of the seed every three hour , walk backward , and you must never tell a soul you 're take it , or it wo n't work .
I would n't spare any of it to any one but you . ''
I felt deeply grateful to Billy , and sorry that I have not like him good .
Somehow , nobody do like Billy Robinson over and above .
But I vow I WOULD like him in future .
I pay him the ten cent cheerfully and take the magic seed a direct , measure myself carefully every day by a mark on the hall door .
I could not see any advance in growth yet , but then I have be take it only three day .
One day the Story Girl have an inspiration .
`` Let u go and ask the Awkward Man and Mr. Campbell for a contribution to the library fund , '' she say .
`` I be sure no one else have ask them , because nobody in Carlisle be relate to them .
Let u all go , and if they give u anything we 'll divide it equally among u . ''
It be a daring proposition , for both Mr. Campbell and the Awkward Man be regard a eccentric personage ; and Mr. Campbell be suppose to detest child .
But where the Story Girl lead we would follow to the death .
The next day be Saturday , we start out in the afternoon .
We take a short cut to Golden Milestone , over a long , green , dewy land full of placid meadow , where sunshine have fall asleep .
At first all be not harmonious .
Felicity be in an ill humour ; she have want to wear her second best dress , but Aunt Janet have decree that her school clothes be good enough to go `` traipse about in the dust . ''
Then the Story Girl arrive , array not in any second best but in her very best dress and hat , which her father have send her from Paris -- a dress of soft , crimson silk , and a white leghorn hat encircle by flame-red poppy .
Neither Felicity nor Cecily could have wear it ; but it become the Story Girl perfectly .
In it she be a thing of fire and laughter and glow , a if the singular charm of her temperament be visible and tangible in it vivid colouring and silken texture .
`` I should n't think you 'd put on your best clothes to go beg for the library in , '' say Felicity cuttingly .
`` Aunt Olivia say that when you be go to have an important interview with a man you ought to look your very best , '' say the Story Girl , give her skirt a lustrous swirl and enjoy the effect .
`` Aunt Olivia spoil you , '' say Felicity .
`` She do n't either , Felicity King !
Aunt Olivia be just sweet .
She kiss me good-night every night , and your mother NEVER kiss you . ''
`` My mother do n't make kiss so common , '' retort Felicity .
`` But she give u pie for dinner every day . ''
`` So do Aunt Olivia . ''
`` Yes , but look at the difference in the size of the piece !
And Aunt Olivia only give you skim milk .
My mother give u cream . ''
`` Aunt Olivia 's skim milk be as good a your mother 's cream , '' cry the Story Girl hotly .
`` Oh , girl , do n't fight , '' say Cecily , the peacemaker .
`` It 's such a nice day , and we 'll have a nice time if you do n't spoil it by fight . ''
`` We 're NOT fight , '' say Felicity .
`` And I like Aunt Olivia .
But my mother be just as good a Aunt Olivia , there now ! ''
`` Of course she be .
Aunt Janet be splendid , '' agree the Story Girl .
They smile at each other amicably .
Felicity and the Story Girl be really quite fond of each other , under the queer surface friction that commonly result from their intercourse .
`` You say once you know a story about the Awkward Man , '' say Felix .
`` You might tell it to u . ''
`` All right , '' agree the Story Girl .
`` The only trouble be , I do n't know the whole story .
But I 'll tell you all I do know .
I call it ` The Mystery of the Golden Milestone . ' ''
`` Oh , I do n't believe that story be true , '' say Felicity .
`` I believe Mrs. Griggs be just romance .
She DOES romance , mother say . ''
`` Yes ; but I do n't believe she could ever have think of such a thing a this herself , so I believe it must be true , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Anyway , this be the story , boy .
You know the Awkward Man have live alone ever since his mother die , ten year ago .
Abel Griggs be his hired man , and he and his wife live in a little house down the Awkward Man 's lane .
Mrs. Griggs make his bread for him , and she clean up his house now and then .
She say he keep it very neat .
But till last fall there be one room she never saw .
It be always lock -- the west one , look out over his garden .
One day last fall the Awkward Man go to Summerside , and Mrs. Griggs scrub his kitchen .
Then she go over the whole house and she try the door of the west room .
Mrs. Griggs be a VERY curious woman .
Uncle Roger say all woman have as much curiosity a be good for them , but Mrs. Griggs have more .
She expect to find the door lock a usual .
It be NOT lock .
She open it and go in .
What do you suppose she find ? ''
`` Something like -- like Bluebeard 's chamber ? ''
suggest Felix in a scared tone .
`` Oh , no , NO !
Nothing like THAT could happen in Prince Edward Island .
But if there HAD be beautiful wife hang up by their hair all round the wall I do n't believe Mrs. Griggs could have be much more astonished .
The room have never be furnish in his mother 's time , but now it be ELEGANTLY furnish , though Mrs. Griggs say SHE do n't know when or how that furniture be bring there .
She say she never saw a room like it in a country farmhouse .
It be like a bed-room and sitting-room combine .
The floor be cover with a carpet like green velvet .
There be fine lace curtain at the window and beautiful picture on the wall .
There be a little white bed , and a dressing-table , a bookcase full of book , a stand with a work basket on it , and a rocking-chair .
There be a woman 's picture above the bookcase .
Mrs. Griggs say she think it be a coloured photograph , but she do n't know who it be .
Anyway , it be a very pretty girl .
But the most amazing thing of all be that A WOMAN 'S DRESS be hang over a chair by the table .
Mrs. Griggs say it NEVER belong to Jasper Dale 's mother , for she think it a sin to wear anything but print and drugget ; and this dress be of PALE BLUE silk .
Besides that , there be a pair of blue satin slipper on the floor beside it -- HIGH-HEELED slipper .
And on the fly-leaves of the book the name ` Alice ' be write .
Now , there never be an Alice in the Dale connection and nobody ever heard of the Awkward Man have a sweetheart .
There , be n't that a lovely mystery ? ''
`` It 's a pretty queer yarn , '' say Felix .
`` I wonder if it be true -- and what it mean . ''
`` I intend to find out what it mean , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I be go to get acquaint with the Awkward Man sometime , and then I 'll find out his Alice-secret . ''
`` I do n't see how you 'll ever get acquaint with him , '' say Felicity .
`` He never go anywhere except to church .
He just stay home and read book when he be n't work .
Mother say he be a perfect hermit . ''
`` I 'll manage it somehow , '' say the Story Girl -- and we have no doubt that she would .
`` But I must wait until I 'm a little old , for he would n't tell the secret of the west room to a little girl .
And I must n't wait till I 'm TOO old , for he be frighten of grown-up girl , because he think they laugh at his awkwardness .
I know I will like him .
He have such a nice face , even if he be awkward .
He look like a man you could tell thing to . ''
`` Well , I 'd like a man who could move around without fall over his own foot , '' say Felicity .
`` And then the look of him !
Uncle Roger say he be long , lank , lean , narrow , and contract . ''
`` Things always sound bad than they be when Uncle Roger say them , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Uncle Edward say Jasper Dale be a very clever man and it 's a great pity he be n't able to finish his college course .
He go to college two year , you know .
Then his father die , and he stay home with his mother because she be very delicate .
I call him a hero .
I wonder if it be true that he write poetry .
Mrs. Griggs say it be .
She say she have see him write it in a brown book .
She say she could n't get near enough to read it , but she know it be poetry by the shape of it . ''
`` Very likely .
If that blue silk dress story be true , I 'd believe ANYTHING of him , '' say Felicity .
We be near Golden Milestone now .
The house be a big , weather-gray structure , overgrown with vine and climb rose .
Something about the three square window in the second story give it an appearance of wink at u in a friendly fashion through it vine -- at least , so the Story Girl say ; and , indeed , we could see it for ourselves after she have once point it out to u .
We do not get into the house , however .
We meet the Awkward man in his yard , and he give u a quarter apiece for our library .
He do not seem awkward or shy ; but then we be only child , and his foot be on his native heath .
He be a tall , slender man , who do not look his forty year , so unwrinkled be his high , white forehead , so clear and lustrous his large , dark-blue eye , so free from silver thread his rather long black hair .
He have large hand and foot , and walk with a slight stoop .
I be afraid we star at him rather rudely while the Story Girl talk to him .
But be not an Awkward Man , who be also a hermit and keep blue silk dress in a locked room , and possibly write poetry , a legitimate object of curiosity ?
I leave it to you .
When we get away we compare note , and find that we all like him -- and this , although he have say little and have appear somewhat glad to get rid of u .
`` He give u the money like a gentleman , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I felt he do n't grudge it .
And now for Mr. Campbell .
It be on HIS account I put on my red silk .
I do n't suppose the Awkward Man notice it at all , but Mr. Campbell will , or I 'm much mistaken . ''
CHAPTER VII .
HOW BETTY SHERMAN WON A HUSBAND The rest of u do not share the Story Girl 's enthusiasm regard our call on Mr. Campbell .
We secretly dread it .
If , a be say , he detest child , who know what sort of a reception we might meet ?
Mr. Campbell be a rich , retired farmer , who take life easily .
He have visit New York and Boston , Toronto and Montreal ; he have even be as far a the Pacific coast .
Therefore he be regard in Carlisle a a much travel man ; and he be know to be `` well read '' and intelligent .
But it be also know that Mr. Campbell be not always in a good humour .
If he like you there be nothing he would not do for you ; if he dislike you -- well , you be not leave in ignorance of it .
In short , we have the impression that Mr. Campbell resemble the famous little girl with the curl in the middle of her forehead .
`` When he be good , he be very , very good , and when he be bad he be horrid . ''
What if this be one of his horrid day ?
`` He ca n't DO anything to u , you know , '' say the Story Girl .
`` He may be rude , but that wo n't hurt any one but himself . ''
`` Hard word break no bone , '' observe Felicity philosophically .
`` But they hurt your feeling .
I be afraid of Mr. Campbell , '' say Cecily candidly .
`` Perhaps we 'd well give up and go home , '' suggest Dan .
`` You can go home if you like , '' say the Story Girl scornfully .
`` But I be go to see Mr. Campbell .
I know I can manage him .
But if I have to go alone , and he give me anything , I 'll keep it all for my own collection , mind you . ''
That settle it .
We be not go to let the Story Girl get ahead of u in the manner of collect .
Mr. Campbell 's housekeeper usher u into his parlour and leave u .
Presently Mr. Campbell himself be stand in the doorway , look u over .
We take heart of grace .
It seem to be one of his good day , for there be a quizzical smile on his broad , clean-shaven , strongly-featured face .
Mr. Campbell be a tall man , with a massive head , well thatch with thick , black hair , gray-streaked .
He have big , black eye , with many wrinkle around them , and a thin , firm , long-lipped mouth .
We think him handsome , for an old man .
His gaze wander over u with uncomplimentary indifference until it fell on the Story Girl , lean back in an arm-chair .
She look like a slender red lily in the unstudied grace of her attitude .
A spark flash into Mr. Campbell 's black eye .
`` Is this a Sunday School deputation ? ''
he inquire rather ironically .
`` No .
We have come to ask a favour of you , '' say the Story Girl .
The magic of her voice work it will on Mr. Campbell , a on all others .
He come in , sit down , hook his thumb into his vest pocket , and smile at her .
`` What be it ? ''
he ask .
`` We be collect for our school library , and we have call to ask you for a contribution , '' she reply .
`` Why should I contribute to your school library ? ''
demand Mr. Campbell .
This be a poser for u .
Why should he , indeed ?
But the Story Girl be quite equal to it .
Leaning forward , and throw an indescribable witchery into tone and eye and smile , she say , `` Because a lady ask you . ''
Mr. Campbell chuckle .
`` The best of all reason , '' he say .
`` But see here , my dear young lady , I 'm an old miser and curmudgeon , a you may have heard .
I HATE to part with my money , even for a good reason .
And I NEVER part with any of it , unless I be to receive some benefit from the expenditure .
Now , what earthly good could I get from your three by six school library ?
None whatever .
But I shall make you a fair offer .
I have hear from my housekeeper 's urchin of a son that you be a ` master hand ' to tell story .
Tell me one , here and now .
I shall pay you in proportion to the entertainment you afford me .
Come now , and do your prettiest . ''
There be a fine mockery in his tone that put the Story Girl on her mettle instantly .
She spring to her foot , an amazing change come over her .
Her eye flash and burn ; crimson spot glow in her cheek .
`` I shall tell you the story of the Sherman girl , and how Betty Sherman win a husband , '' she say .
We gasp .
Was the Story Girl crazy ?
Or have she forget that Betty Sherman be Mr. Campbell 's own great-grandmother , and that her method of win a husband be not exactly in accordance with maidenly tradition .
But Mr. Campbell chuckle again .
`` An excellent test , '' he say .
`` If you can amuse ME with that story you must be a wonder .
I 've hear it so often that it have no more interest for me than the alphabet . ''
`` One cold winter day , eighty year ago , '' begin the Story Girl without further parley , `` Donald Fraser be sit by the window of his new house , play his fiddle for company , and look out over the white , frozen bay before his door .
It be bitter , bitter cold , and a storm be brew .
But , storm , or no storm , Donald mean to go over the bay that even to see Nancy Sherman .
He be think of her a he play ` Annie Laurie , ' for Nancy be more beautiful than the lady of the song .
` Her face , it be the fair that e'er the sun shone on , ' hum Donald -- and oh , he think so , too !
He do not know whether Nancy care for him or not .
He have many rival .
But he know that if she would not come to be the mistress of his new house no one else ever should .
So he sit there that afternoon and dreamed of her , a he play sweet old song and rollick jig on his fiddle .
`` While he be play a sleigh drive up to the door , and Neil Campbell come in .
Donald be not overly glad to see him , for he suspect where he be go .
Neil Campbell , who be Highland Scotch and live down at Berwick , be court Nancy Sherman , too ; and , what be far bad , Nancy 's father favour him , because he be a rich man than Donald Fraser .
But Donald be not go to show all he think -- Scotch people never do -- and he pretend to be very glad to see Neil and make him heartily welcome .
`` Neil sit down by the roaring fire , look quite well satisfied with himself .
It be ten mile from Berwick to the bay shore , and a call at a half way house be just the thing .
Then Donald bring out the whisky .
They always do that eighty year ago , you know .
If you be a woman , you could give your visitor a dish of tea ; but if you be a man and do not offer them a ` taste ' of whisky , you be think either very mean or very ignorant . ''
` You look cold , ' say Donald , in his great , hearty voice .
` Sit nearer the fire , man , and put a bit of warmth in your vein .
It 's bitter cold the day .
And now tell me the Berwick news .
Has Jean McLean make up with her man yet ?
And be it true that Sandy McQuarrie be to marry Kate Ferguson ?
` Twill be a match now !
Sure , with her red hair , Sandy will not be like to lose his bride past find . '
`` Neil have plenty of news to tell .
And the more whisky he drink the more he tell .
He do n't notice that Donald be not take much .
Neil talk on and on , and of course he soon begin to tell thing it would have be much wiser not to tell .
Finally he tell Donald that he be go over the bay to ask Nancy Sherman that very night to marry him .
And if she would have him , then Donald and all the folk should see a wedding that WAS a wedding .
`` Oh , be n't Donald take aback !
This be more than he have expect .
Neil have n't be court Nancy very long , and Donald never dream he would propose to her QUITE so soon .
`` At first Donald do n't know what to do .
He felt sure deep down in his heart , that Nancy like HIM .
She be very shy and modest , but you know a girl can let a man see she like him without go out of her way .
But Donald know that if Neil propose first he would have the best chance .
Neil be rich and the Shermans be poor , and old Elias Sherman would have the most to say in the matter .
If he tell Nancy she must take Neil Campbell she would never dream of disobey him .
Old Elias Sherman be a man who have to be obey .
But if Nancy have only promise some one else first her father would not make her break her word .
`` Was n't it a hard plight for poor Donald ?
But he be a Scotchman , you know , and it 's pretty hard to stick a Scotchman long .
Presently a twinkle come into his eye , for he remember that all be fair in love and war .
So he say to Neil , oh , so persuasively , '' ` Have some more , man , have some more .
` Twill keep the heart in you in the teeth of that wind .
Help yourself .
There 's plenty more where that come from . '
`` Neil do n't want MUCH persuasion .
He take some more , and say slyly , '' ` Is it go over the bay the night that yourself will be do ? '
`` Donald shake his head . '' '
I have think of it , ' he own , ` but it look a wee like a storm , and my sleigh be at the blacksmith 's to be shoe .
If I go it must be on Black Dan 's back , and he like a canter over the ice in a snow-storm as little a I . His own fireside be the best place for a man to-night , Campbell .
Have another taste , man , have another taste . '
`` Neil go on ` tasting , ' and that sly Donald sit there with a sober face , but laugh eye , and coax him on .
At last Neil 's head fell forward on his breast , and he be sound asleep .
Donald get up , put on his overcoat and cap , and go to the door . ''
` May your sleep be long and sweet , man , ' he say , laugh softly , ` and a for the waking , ` twill be betwixt you and me . '
`` With that he untie Neil 's horse , climb into Neil 's sleigh , and tuck Neil 's buffalo robe about him . ''
` Now , Bess , old girl , do your bonny , ' he say .
` There 's more than you know hang on your speed .
If the Campbell wake too soon Black Dan could show you a pair of clean heel for all your good start .
On , my girl . '
`` Brown Bess go over the ice like a deer , and Donald keep thinking of what he should say to Nancy -- and more still of what she would say to him .
SUPPOSE he be mistake .
SUPPOSE she say ` no ! ' ''
` Neil would have the laugh on me then .
Sure he 's sleep well .
And the snow be come soon .
There 'll be a bonny swirl on the bay ere long .
I hope no harm will come to the lad if he start to cross .
When he wake he 'll be in such a fine Highland temper that he 'll never stop to think of danger .
Well , Bess , old girl , here we be .
Now , Donald Fraser , pluck up heart and play the man .
Never flinch because a slip of a lass look scornful at you out of the bonny dark-blue eye on earth . '
`` But in spite of his bold word Donald 's heart be thump a he drive into the Sherman yard .
Nancy be there milk a cow by the stable door , but she stand up when she saw Donald come .
Oh , she be very beautiful !
Her hair be like a skein of golden silk , and her eye be as blue a the gulf water when the sun break out after a storm .
Donald felt more nervous than ever .
But he know he must make the most of his chance .
He might not see Nancy alone again before Neil come .
He catch her hand and stammer out , '' ` Nan , lass , I love you .
You may think 't be a hasty wooing , but that 's a story I can tell you later maybe .
I know well I 'm not worthy of you , but if true love could make a man worthy there 'd be none before me .
Will you have me , Nan ? '
`` Nancy do n't SAY she would have him .
She just LOOKED it , and Donald kiss her right there in the snow .
`` The next morning the storm be over .
Donald know Neil must be soon on his track .
He do not want to make the Sherman house the scene of a quarrel , so he resolve to get away before the Campbell come .
He persuade Nancy to go with him to visit some friend in another settlement .
As he bring Neil 's sleigh up to the door he saw a black speck far out on the bay and laugh . ''
` Black Dan go well , but he 'll not be quick enough , ' he say .
`` Half an hour later Neil Campbell rush into the Sherman kitchen and oh , how angry he be !
There be nobody there but Betty Sherman , and Betty be not afraid of him .
She be never afraid of anybody .
She be very handsome , with hair as brown a October nut and black eye and crimson cheek ; and she have always be in love with Neil Campbell herself . ''
` Good morning , Mr. Campbell , ' she say , with a toss of her head .
` It 's early abroad you be .
And on Black Dan , no le !
Was I mistake in thinking that Donald Fraser say once that his favourite horse should never be back by any man but him ?
But doubtless a fair exchange be no robbery , and Brown Bess be a good mare in her way . ' ''
` Where be Donald Fraser ? '
say Neil , shake his fist .
` It 's him I 'm seek , and it 's him I will be find .
Where be he , Betty Sherman ? ' ''
` Donald Fraser be far enough away by this time , ' mock Betty .
` He be a prudent fellow , and have some quickness of wit under that sandy thatch of his .
He come here last night at sunset , with a horse and sleigh not his own , or lately gotten , and he ask Nan in the stable yard to marry him .
Did a man ask ME to marry him at the cow 's side with a milk pail in my hand , it 's a cold answer he 'd get for his pain .
But Nan think differently , and they sit late together last night , and 't be a bonny story Nan waken me to hear when she come to bed -- the story of a braw lover who let his secret out when the whisky be above the wit , and then fell asleep while his rival be away to woo and win his lass .
Did you ever hear a like story , Mr. Campbell ? ' ''
` Oh , yes , ' say Neil fiercely .
` It be laugh at me over the country side and tell that story that Donald Fraser will be do , be it ?
But when I meet him it be not laugh he will be do .
Oh , no .
There will be another story to tell ! ' ''
` Now , do n't meddle with the man , ' cry Betty .
` What a state to be in because one good-looking lass like sandy hair and gray eye well than Highland black and blue !
You have not the spirit of a wren , Neil Campbell .
Were I you , I would show Donald Fraser that I could woo and win a lass as speedily a any Lowlander of them all ; that I would !
There 's many a girl would gladly say ` yes ' for your asking .
And here stand one !
Why not marry ME , Neil Campbell ?
Folks say I 'm as bonny a Nan -- and I could love you as well a Nan love her Donald -- ay , and ten time well ! '
`` What do you suppose the Campbell do ?
Why , just the thing he ought to have do .
He take Betty at her word on the spot ; and there be a double wedding soon after .
And it be say that Neil and Betty be the happy couple in the world -- happy even than Donald and Nancy .
So all be well because it end well ! ''
The Story Girl curtsy until her silken skirt sweep the floor .
Then she fling herself in her chair and look at Mr. Campbell , flush , triumphant , dare .
The story be old to u .
It have once be publish in a Charlottetown paper , and we have read in Aunt Olivia 's scrapbook , where the Story Girl have learn it .
But we have listen entrance .
I have write down the bare word of the story , a she tell it ; but I can never reproduce the charm and colour and spirit she infuse into it .
It LIVED for u .
Donald and Neil , Nancy and Betty , be there in that room with u .
We saw the flash of expression on their face , we hear their voice , angry or tender , mock or merry , in Lowland and Highland accent .
We realize all the mingle coquetry and feeling and defiance and archness in Betty Sherman 's dare speech .
We have even forget all about Mr. Campbell .
That gentleman , in silence , take out his wallet , extract a note therefrom , and hand it gravely to the Story Girl .
`` There be five dollar for you , '' he say , `` and your story be well worth it .
You ARE a wonder .
Some day you will make the world realize it .
I 've be about a bit , and hear some good thing , but I 've never enjoy anything more than that threadbare old story I hear in my cradle .
And now , will you do me a favour ? ''
`` Of course , '' say the delighted Story Girl .
`` Recite the multiplication table for me , '' say Mr. Campbell .
We star .
Well might Mr. Campbell be call eccentric .
What on earth do he want the multiplication table recite for ?
Even the Story Girl be surprise .
But she begin promptly , with twice one and go through it to twelve time twelve .
She repeat it simply , but her voice change from one tone to another a each in succession grow tire .
We have never dream that there be so much in the multiplication table .
As she announce it , the fact that three time three be nine be exquisitely ridiculous , five time six almost brought tear to our eye , eight time seven be the most tragic and frightful thing ever heard of , and twelve time twelve rang like a trumpet call to victory .
Mr. Campbell nod his satisfaction .
`` I think you could do it , '' he say .
`` The other day I find this statement in a book .
` Her voice would have make the multiplication table charm ! '
I think of it when I hear yours .
I do n't believe it before , but I do now . ''

CHAPTER X .

`` Indeed , I would if I just make up my mind to .
Why not ?
Why not bare foot -- if they 're clean -- as well a bare hand and face ? ''
`` Oh , you would n't !
It would be such a disgrace ! ''
say poor Felicity in real distress .
`` We go to school barefooted all June , '' argue that wicked Story Girl .
`` What be the difference between go to the schoolhouse barefooted in the daytime and go in the evening ? ''
`` Oh , there 's EVERY difference .
I ca n't just explain it -- but every one KNOWS there be a difference .
You know it yourself .
Oh , PLEASE , do n't do such a thing , Sara . ''
`` Well , I wo n't , just to oblige you , '' say the Story Girl , who would have die the death before she would have go to a `` public meeting '' barefooted .
We be all rather excite over the magic lantern show which an itinerant lecturer be to give in the schoolhouse that even .
Even Felix and I , who have see such show galore , be interested , and the rest be quite wild .
There have never be such a thing in Carlisle before .
We be all go , Peter include .
Peter go everywhere with u now .
He be a regular attendant at church and Sunday School , where his behaviour be as irreproachable a if he have be `` raise '' in the caste of Vere de Vere .
It be feather in the Story Girl 's cap , for she take all the credit of have start Peter on the right road .

But Peter 's stocking be always darn .

I s ` pose it 's just the same , even if it be old , be n't it ? ''
`` Oh , yes , '' Cecily have assure him .
`` The Bible be always the same . ''

But I hide then .
Sara just go and cry in public . ''

And I 've never see a magic lantern -- I 've never see ANYTHING . ''

`` If there be we would n't be allow to go . ''

`` Maybe I 'd be of some importance to ma then . ''

`` Perhaps she 'd let you go then .
She like Cecily .
She do n't like either Felicity or me , so it would only make matter bad for u to try . ''
`` Ma 's go to town -- pa and her go this afternoon -- and they 're not come back till to-morrow .
There 's nobody home but Judy Pineau and me . ''

Your mother wo n't ever know , if you coax Judy to hold her tongue . ''
`` Oh , but that 's wrong , '' say Felicity .
`` You should n't put Sara up to disobey her mother . ''
Now , Felicity for once be undoubtedly right .
The Story Girl 's suggestion WAS wrong ; and if it have be Cecily who protest , the Story Girl would probably have listen to her , and proceed no further in the matter .
But Felicity be one of those unfortunate people whose protest against wrong-doing serve only to drive the wrong-doer further on her sinful way .

The rest of u hold our tongue .
It be , we tell ourselves , Sara 's own lookout .
`` I have a good mind to do it , '' say Sara .
`` but I ca n't get my good clothes ; they 're in the spare room , and ma lock the door , for fear somebody would get at the fruit cake .
I have n't a single thing to wear , except my school gingham . ''
`` Well , that 's new and pretty , '' say the Story Girl .
`` We 'll lend you some thing .
You can have my lace collar .
That 'll make the gingham quite elegant .
And Cecily will lend you her second best hat . ''
`` But I 've no shoe or stocking .
They 're lock up too . ''

Sara do yield .
When the Story Girl 's voice entreat it be not easy to resist it temptation , even if you want to .

Felicity say aside .

The lecturer be go to Markdale next week .

It be a cool , dewy evening , and we walk down the long , red hill in the high of spirit .
Over a valley fill with beech and spruce be a sunset afterglow -- creamy yellow and a hue that be not so much red a the dream of red , with a young moon swing low in it .
The air be sweet with the breath of mown hayfield where swath of clover have be steep in the sun .

Those of u who have nothing the matter with our conscience enjoy our walk to the little whitewashed schoolhouse in the valley .

The Story Girl herself be not altogether at ease .
Probably her own conscience be trouble her .
But admit it she would not .
`` Now , Sara , '' she say , `` you just take my advice and go into this with all your heart if you go at all .
Never mind if it be bad .
There 's no use be naughty if you spoil your fun by wish all the time you be good .
You can repent afterwards , but there be no use in mix the two thing together . ''
`` I 'm not repent , '' protest Sara .
`` I 'm only scar of ma find it out . ''
`` Oh ! ''
The Story Girl 's voice express her scorn .
For remorse she have understanding and sympathy ; but fear of her fellow creature be something unknown to her .
`` Did n't Judy Pineau promise you solemnly she would n't tell ? ''
`` Yes ; but maybe some one who see me there will mention it to ma . ''

It be n't too late .

But Sara could not give up the delight of the show .
So she walk on , a small , miserable testimony that the way of the transgressor be never easy , even when say transgressor be only a damsel of eleven .
The magic lantern show be a splendid one .
The view be good and the lecturer witty .

Sara , who have not enjoy the exhibition at all , seem to feel more cheerful when it be over and she be go home .

But she do n't .
I could see that .
So I 've do wrong and make her do wrong -- and there 's nothing to show for it . ''
The night be scent and mysterious .
The wind be play an eerie fleshless melody in the reed of the brook hollow .
The sky be dark and starry , and across it the Milky Way fling it shimmer misty ribbon .
`` There 's four hundred million star in the Milky Way , '' quoth Peter , who frequently astonish u by know more than any hired boy could be expect to .
He have a retentive memory , and never forget anything he hear or read .

She have not do so before because he be barefooted .
It be permissible for hired boy to go to public meeting -- when not hold in the church -- with bare foot , and no particular disgrace attach to it .
But Felicity would not walk with a barefooted companion .
It be dark now , so nobody would notice his foot .
`` I know a story about the Milky Way , '' say the Story Girl , brighten up .
`` I read it in a book of Aunt Louisa 's in town , and I learn it off by heart .
Once there be two archangel in heaven , name Zerah and Zulamith -- '' `` Have angel names -- same a people ? ''
interrupt Peter .
`` Yes , of course .
They MUST have .
They 'd be all mixed up if they have n't . ''

`` No .
You 'll have a new name up there , '' say Cecily gently .
`` It say so in the Bible . ''

Peter would be such a funny name for an angel .

`` Oh , archangel be angel that have be angel so long that they 've have time to grow good and bright and more beautiful than new angel , '' say the Story Girl , who probably make that explanation up on the spur of the moment , just to pacify Peter .
`` How long do it take for an angel to grow into an archangel ? ''
pursue Peter .
`` Oh , I do n't know .
Millions of year likely .
And even then I do n't suppose ALL the angel do .

`` I shall be satisfy just to be a plain angel , '' say Felicity modestly .
`` Oh , see here , if you 're go to interrupt and argue over everything , we 'll never get the story tell , '' say Felix .
`` Dry up , all of you , and let the Story Girl go on . ''
We dry up , and the Story Girl go on .
`` Zerah and Zulamith love each other , just a mortal love , and this be forbid by the law of the Almighty .
And because Zerah and Zulamith have so broken God 's law they be banish from His presence to the uttermost bound of the universe .
If they have be banish TOGETHER it would have be no punishment ; so Zerah be exile to a star on one side of the universe , and Zulamith be send to a star on the other side of the universe ; and between them be a fathomless abyss which think itself could not cross .
Only one thing could cross it -- and that be love .
Zulamith yearn for Zerah with such fidelity and longing that he begin to build up a bridge of light from his star ; and Zerah , not know this , but love and long for him , begin to build a similar bridge of light from her star .
For a thousand thousand year they both build the bridge of light , and at last they meet and spring into each other 's arm .
Their toil and loneliness and suffering be all over and forget , and the bridge they have build span the gulf between their star of exile .
`` Now , when the other archangel saw what have be do they fly in fear and anger to God 's white throne , and cry to Him , '' ` See what these rebellious one have do !
They have build them a bridge of light across the universe , and set Thy decree of separation at naught .
Do Thou , then , stretch forth Thine arm and destroy their impious work . '
`` They cease -- and all heaven be hush .
Through the silence sound the voice of the Almighty . ''
` Nay , ' He say , ` whatsoever in my universe true love hath build not even the Almighty can destroy .
The bridge must stand forever . '
`` And , '' conclude the Story Girl , her face upturned to the sky and her big eye fill with starlight , `` it stand still .
That bridge be the Milky Way . ''
`` What a lovely story , '' sigh Sara Ray , who have be woo to a temporary forgetfulness of her woe by it charm .
The rest of u come back to earth , feel that we have be wander among the host of heaven .
We be not old enough to appreciate fully the wonderful meaning of the legend ; but we felt it beauty and it appeal .
To u forevermore the Milky Way would be , not Peter 's overwhelming garland of sun , but the lucent bridge , love-created , on which the banished archangel cross from star to star .
We have to go up Sara Ray 's lane with her to her very door , for she be afraid Peg Bowen would catch her if she go alone .
Then the Story Girl and I walk up the hill together .
Peter and Felicity lag behind .
Cecily and Dan and Felix be walk before u , hand in hand , sing a hymn .
Cecily have a very sweet voice , and I listen in delight .
But the Story Girl sigh .
`` What if Sara do take the measles ? ''
she ask miserably .
`` Everyone have to have the measles sometime , '' I say comfortingly , `` and the young you be the good . ''
CHAPTER XI .
THE STORY GIRL DOES PENANCE Ten day later , Aunt Olivia and Uncle Roger go to town one evening , to remain over night , and the next day .
Peter and the Story Girl be to stay at Uncle Alec 's during their absence .
We be in the orchard at sunset , listen to the story of King Cophetua and the beggar maid -- all of u , except Peter , who be hoe turnip , and Felicity , who have go down the hill on an errand to Mrs. Ray .
The Story Girl impersonate the beggar maid so vividly , and with such an illusion of beauty , that we do not wonder in the least at the king 's love for her .
I have read the story before , and it have be my opinion that it be `` rot . ''
No king , I felt certain , would ever marry a beggar maid when he have princess galore from whom to choose .
But now I understand it all .
When Felicity return we conclude from her expression that she have news .
And she have .
`` Sara be real sick , '' she say , with regret , and something that be not regret mingle in her voice .
`` She have a cold and sore throat , and she be feverish .
Mrs. Ray say if she be n't well by the morning she 's go to send for the doctor .
AND SHE IS AFRAID IT 'S THE MEASLES . ''
Felicity fling the last sentence at the Story Girl , who turn very pale .
`` Oh , do you suppose she catch them at the magic lantern show ? ''
she say miserably .
`` Where else could she have catch them ? ''

`` I do n't see her , of course -- Mrs. Ray meet me at the door and tell me not to come in .

Of course , '' add Felicity , her heart melting at sight of the misery in the Story Girl 's piteous eye , `` Mrs. Ray always look on the dark side , and it may not be the measles Sara have after all . ''
But Felicity have do her work too thoroughly .
The Story Girl be not to be comfort .
`` I 'd give anything if I 'd never put Sara up to go to that show , '' she say .

I sha 'n ' t sleep a wink to-night . ''
I do n't think she do .
She look very pale and woebegone when she come down to breakfast .
But , for all that , there be a certain exhilaration about her .
`` I 'm go to do penance all day for coax Sara to disobey her mother , '' she announce with chastened triumph .
`` Penance ? ''
we murmur in bewilderment .
`` Yes .
I 'm go to deny myself everything I like , and do everything I can think of that I do n't like , just to punish myself for be so wicked .
And if any of you think of anything I do n't , just mention it to me .
I think it out last night .
Maybe Sara wo n't be so very sick if God see I 'm truly sorry . ''
`` He can see it anyhow , without you 're do anything , '' say Cecily .
`` Well , my conscience will feel well . ''

`` I never hear of one do it . ''
But the rest of u rather look with favour on the Story Girl 's idea .
We felt sure that she would do penance a picturesquely and thoroughly a she do everything else .
`` You might put pea in your shoe , you know , '' suggest Peter .
`` The very thing !
I never think of that .
I 'll get some after breakfast .
I 'm not go to eat a single thing all day , except bread and water -- and not much of that ! ''
This , we felt , be a heroic measure indeed .
To sit down to one of Aunt Janet 's meal , in ordinary health and appetite , and eat nothing but bread and water -- that would be penance with a vengeance !
We felt WE could never do it .
But the Story Girl do it .
We admire and pity her .
But now I do not think that she either need our pity or deserve our admiration .
Her ascetic fare be really sweet to her than honey of Hymettus .
She be , though quite unconsciously , act a part , and taste all the subtle joy of the artist , which be so much more exquisite than any material pleasure .
Aunt Janet , of course , notice the Story Girl 's abstinence and ask if she be sick .
`` No .
I be just do penance , Aunt Janet , for a sin I commit .
I ca n't confess it , because that would bring trouble on another person .
So I 'm go to do penance all day .
You do n't mind , do you ? ''
Aunt Janet be in a very good humour that morning , so she merely laugh .
`` Not if you do n't go too far with your nonsense , '' she say tolerantly .
`` Thank you .
And will you give me a handful of hard pea after breakfast , Aunt Janet ?
I want to put them in my shoe . ''
`` There be n't any ; I use the last in the soup yesterday . ''
`` Oh ! ''
The Story Girl be much disappointed .
`` Then I suppose I 'll have to do without .
The new pea would n't hurt enough .
They 're so soft they 'd just squash flat . ''
`` I 'll tell you , '' say Peter , `` I 'll pick up a lot of those little round pebble on Mr. King 's front walk .
They 'll be just as good a pea . ''
`` You 'll do nothing of the sort , '' say Aunt Janet .
`` Sara must not do penance in that way .
She would wear hole in her stocking , and might seriously bruise her foot . ''
`` What would you say if I take a whip and whip my bare shoulder till the blood come ? ''
demand the Story Girl aggrieve .
`` I would n't SAY anything , '' retort Aunt Janet .
`` I 'd simply turn you over my knee and give you a sound , solid spanking , Miss Sara .
You 'd find that penance enough . ''
The Story Girl be crimson with indignation .
To have such a remark make to you -- when you be fourteen and a half -- and before the boy , too !
Really , Aunt Janet could be very dreadful .
It be vacation , and there be not much to do that day ; we be soon free to seek the orchard .
But the Story Girl would not come .
She have seat herself in the darkest , hot corner of the kitchen , with a piece of old cotton in her hand .

Aunt Janet wo n't let me put pebble in my shoe , but I 've put a thistle next my skin on my back and it stick into me if I lean back the least bit .
And I 'm go to work buttonhole all over this cotton .
I hate work buttonhole bad than anything in the world , so I 'm go to work them all day . ''
`` What 's the good of work buttonhole on an old rag ? ''
ask Felicity .
`` It be n't any good .
The beauty of penance be that it make you feel uncomfortable .
So it do n't matter what you do , whether it 's useful or not , so long a it 's nasty .
Oh , I wonder how Sara be this morning . ''
`` Mother 's go down this afternoon , '' say Felicity .
`` She say none of u must go near the place till we know whether it be the measles or not . ''
`` I 've think of a great penance , '' say Cecily eagerly .
`` Do n't go to the missionary meeting to-night . ''
The Story Girl look piteous .
`` I think of that myself -- but I CA N'T stay home , Cecily .
It would be more than flesh and blood could endure .
I MUST hear that missionary speak .
They say he be all but eat by cannibal once .
Just think how many new story I 'd have to tell after I 'd hear him !

I 'll wear my school dress and hat .
THAT will be penance .
Felicity , when you set the table for dinner , put the broken-handled knife for me .
I hate it so .
And I 'm go to take a dose of Mexican Tea every two hour .
It 's such dreadful taste stuff -- but it 's a good blood purifier , so Aunt Janet ca n't object to it . ''
The Story Girl carry out her self-imposed penance fully .
All day she sit in the kitchen and work buttonhole , subsist on bread and water and Mexican Tea .
Felicity do a mean thing .
She go to work and make little raisin pie , right there in the kitchen before the Story Girl .
The smell of raisin pie be something to tempt an anchorite ; and the Story Girl be exceedingly fond of them .
Felicity eat two in her very presence , and then bring the rest out to u in the orchard .
The Story Girl could see u through the window , carouse without stint on raisin pie and Uncle Edward 's cherry .
But she work on at her buttonhole .
She would not look at the excite serial in the new magazine Dan bring home from the post-office , neither would she open a letter from her father .
Pat come over , but his most seductive purr win no notice from his mistress , who refuse herself the pleasure of even pat him .
