Mr. Millward be a doctor , and Mrs. Millward be a B.A . Aunt Janet be very desirous that everything should be as nice a possible , and we be all send to our room before tea to wash and dress up .
The Story Girl slip over home , and when she come back we gasp .
She have comb her hair out straight , and braid it in a tight , kinky , pudgy braid ; and she wear an old dress of faded print , with hole in the elbow and ragged flounce , which be much too short for her .
`` Sara Stanley , have you take leave of your sens ? ''
demanded Aunt Janet .
`` What do you mean by put on such a rig !
Do n't you know I have company to tea ? ''
`` Yes , and that be just why I put it on , Aunt Janet .
I want to mortify the flesh -- '' `` I 'll ` mortify ' you , if I catch you show yourself to the Millwards like that , my girl !
Go right home and dress yourself decently -- or eat your supper in the kitchen . ''
The Story Girl choose the latter alternative .
She be highly indignant .
I verily believe that to sit at the dining-room table , in that shabby , outgrown dress , conscious of look her ugliest , and eat only bread and water before the critical Millwards would have be positive bliss to her .
When we go to the missionary meeting that evening , the Story Girl wear her school dress and hat , while Felicity and Cecily be in their pretty muslin .
And she have tie her hair with a snuff-brown ribbon which be very unbecoming to her .
The first person we saw in the church porch be Mrs. Ray .
She tell u that Sara have nothing bad than a feverish cold .
The missionary have at least seven happy listener that night .
We be all glad that Sara do not have measles , and the Story Girl be radiant .
`` Now you see all your penance be waste , '' say Felicity , a we walk home , keep close together because of the rumour that Peg Bowen be abroad .
`` Oh , I do n't know .
I feel well since I punish myself .
But I 'm go to make up for it to-morrow , '' say the Story Girl energetically .
`` In fact , I 'll begin to-night .
I 'm go to the pantry as soon a I get home , and I 'll read father 's letter before I go to bed .
Was n't the missionary splendid ?
That cannibal story be simply grand .
I try to remember every word , so that I can tell it just a he tell it .
Missionaries be such noble people . ''
`` I 'd like to be a missionary and have adventure like that , '' say Felix .
`` It would be all right if you could be sure the cannibal would be interrupt in the nick of time a his be , '' say Dan .
`` But sposen they be n't ? ''
`` Nothing would prevent cannibal from eat Felix if they once catch him , '' giggle Felicity .
`` He 's so nice and fat . ''
I be sure Felix felt very unlike a missionary at that precise moment .
`` I 'm go to put two cent more a week in my missionary box than I 've be do , '' say Cecily determinedly .
Two cent more a week out of Cecily 's egg money , mean something of a sacrifice .
It inspire the rest of u .
We all decide to increase our weekly contribution by a cent or so .
And Peter , who have have no missionary box at all , up to this time , determine to start one .
`` I do n't seem to be able to feel a int ` rest in missionary a you folks do , '' he say , `` but maybe if I begin to give something I 'll get int ` rest .
I 'll want to know how my money 's be spend .
I wo n't be able to give much .
When your father 's run away , and your mother go out wash , and you 're only old enough to get fifty cent a week , you ca n't give much to the heathen .
But I 'll do the best I can .
My Aunt Jane be fond of mission .
Are there any Methodist heathen ?
I s ` pose I ought to give my box to them , rather than to Presbyterian heathen . ''
`` No , it 's only after they 're convert that they 're anything in particular , '' say Felicity .
`` Before that , they 're just plain heathen .
But if you want your money to go to a Methodist missionary you can give it to the Methodist minister at Markdale .
I guess the Presbyterians can get along without it , and look after their own heathen . ''
`` Just smell Mrs. Sampson 's flower , '' say Cecily , a we pass a trim white pal close to the road , over which blow odour sweeter than the perfume of Araby 's shore .
`` Her rose be all out and that bed of Sweet William be a sight by daylight . ''
`` Sweet William be a dreadful name for a flower , '' say the Story Girl .
`` William be a man 's name , and men be NEVER sweet .
They be a great many nice thing , but they be NOT sweet and should n't be .
That be for woman .
Oh , look at the moonshine on the road in that gap between the spruce !
I 'd like a dress of moonshine , with star for button . ''
`` It would n't do , '' say Felicity decidedly .
`` You could see through it . ''
Which seem to settle the question of moonshine dress effectually .
CHAPTER XII .
THE BLUE CHEST OF RACHEL WARD `` It 's utterly out of the question , '' say Aunt Janet seriously .
When Aunt Janet say seriously that anything be out of the question it mean that she be think about it , and would probably end up by do it .
If a thing really be out of the question she merely laugh and refuse to discuss it at all .
The particular matter in or out of the question that open day of August be a project which Uncle Edward have recently moot .
Uncle Edward 's young daughter be to be marry ; and Uncle Edward have write over , urge Uncle Alec , Aunt Janet and Aunt Olivia to go down to Halifax for the wedding and spend a week there .
Uncle Alec and Aunt Olivia be eager to go ; but Aunt Janet at first declare it be impossible .
`` How could we go away and leave the place to the mercy of all those young one ? ''
she demand .
`` We 'd come home and find them all sick , and the house burn down . ''
`` Not a bit of fear of it , '' scoff Uncle Roger .
`` Felicity be as good a housekeeper a you be ; and I shall be here to look after them all , and keep them from burn the house down .
You 've be promise Edward for year to visit him , and you 'll never have a good chance .
The haying be over and harvest be n't on , and Alec need a change .
He be n't look well at all . ''
I think it be Uncle Roger 's last argument which convince Aunt Janet .
In the end she decide to go .
Uncle Roger 's house be to be close , and he and Peter and the Story Girl be to take up their abode with u .
We be all delight .
Felicity , in especial , seem to be in seventh heaven .
To be leave in sole charge of a big house , with three meal a day to plan and prepare , with poultry and cow and dairy and garden to superintend , apparently furnish forth Felicity 's conception of Paradise .
Of course , we be all to help ; but Felicity be to `` run thing , '' and she glory in it .
The Story Girl be pleased , too .
`` Felicity be go to give me cook lesson , '' she confide to me , a we walk in the orchard .
`` Is n't that fine ?
It will be easy when there be no grown-ups around to make me nervous , and laugh if I make mistake . ''
Uncle Alec and aunt leave on Monday morning .
Poor Aunt Janet be full of dismal foreboding , and give u so many charge and warning that we do not try to remember any of them ; Uncle Alec merely tell u to be good and mind what Uncle Roger say .
Aunt Olivia laugh at u out of her pansy-blue eye , and tell u she know exactly what we felt like and hop we 'd have a gorgeous time .
`` Mind they go to bed at a decent hour , '' Aunt Janet call back to Uncle Roger a she drive out of the gate .
`` And if anything dreadful happen telegraph u . ''
Then they be really go and we be all leave `` to keep house . ''
Uncle Roger and Peter go away to their work .
Felicity at once set the preparation for dinner a-going , and allot to each of u his portion of service .
The Story Girl be to prepare the potato ; Felix and Dan be to pick and shell the pea ; Cecily be to attend the fire ; I be to peel the turnip .
Felicity make our mouth water by announce that she be go to make a roly-poly jam pudding for dinner .
I peel my turnip on the back porch , put them in their pot , and set them on the stove .
Then I be at liberty to watch the others , who have long job .
The kitchen be a scene of happy activity .
The Story Girl peel her potato , somewhat slowly and awkwardly -- for she be not deft at household task ; Dan and Felix shell pea and torment Pat by attach pod to his ear and tail ; Felicity , flush and serious , measure and stir skilfully .
`` I be sit on a tragedy , '' say the Story Girl suddenly .
Felix and I star .
We be not quite sure what a `` tragedy '' be , but we do not think it be an old blue wooden chest , such a the Story Girl be undoubtedly sit on , if eyesight count for anything .
The old chest fill up the corner between the table and the wall .
Neither Felix nor I have ever think about it particularly .
It be very large and heavy , and Felicity generally say hard thing of it when she sweep the kitchen .
`` This old blue chest hold a tragedy , '' explain the Story Girl .
`` I know a story about it . ''
`` Cousin Rachel Ward 's wedding thing be all in that old chest , '' say Felicity .
Who be Cousin Rachel Ward ?
And why be her wed thing shut up in an old blue chest in Uncle Alec 's kitchen ?
We demand the tale instantly .
The Story Girl tell it to u a she peel her potato .
Perhaps the potato suffer -- Felicity declare the eye be not properly do at all -- but the story do not .
`` It be a sad story , '' say the Story Girl , `` and it happen fifty year ago , when Grandfather and Grandmother King be quite young .
Grandmother 's cousin Rachel Ward come to spend a winter with them .
She belong to Montreal and she be an orphan too , just like the Family Ghost .
I have never hear what she look like , but she MUST have be beautiful , of course . ''
`` Mother say she be awful sentimental and romantic , '' interject Felicity .
`` Well , anyway , she meet Will Montague that winter .
He be handsome -- everybody say so '' -- `` And an awful flirt , '' say Felicity .
`` Felicity , I WISH you would n't interrupt .
It spoil the effect .
What would you feel like if I go and keep stir thing that do n't belong to it into that pudding ?
I feel just the same way .
Well , Will Montague fell in love with Rachel Ward , and she with him , and it be all arrange that they be to be marry from here in the spring .
Poor Rachel be so happy that winter ; she make all her wedding thing with her own hand .
Girls do , then , you know , for there be no such thing a a sewing-machine .
Well , at last in April the wedding day come , and all the guest be here , and Rachel be dress in her wedding robe , wait for her bridegroom .
And '' -- the Story Girl lay down her knife and potato and clasp her wet hand -- `` WILL MONTAGUE NEVER CAME ! ''
We felt a much of a shock a if we have be one of the expectant guest ourselves .
`` What happen to him ?
Was HE kill too ? ''
ask Felix .
The Story Girl sigh and resume her work .
`` No , indeed .
I wish he have be .
THAT would have be suitable and romantic .
No , it be just something horrid .
He have to run away for debt !
Fancy !
He act mean right through , Aunt Janet say .
He never send even a word to Rachel , and she never hear from him again . ''
`` Pig ! ''
say Felix forcibly .
`` She be broken-hearted of course .
When she find out what have happen , she take all her wedding thing , and her supply of linen , and some present that have be give her , and pack them all away in this old blue chest .
Then she go away back to Montreal , and take the key with her .
She never come back to the Island again -- I suppose she could n't bear to .
And she have live in Montreal ever since and never marry .
She be an old woman now -- nearly seventy-five .
And this chest have never be open since . ''
`` Mother write to Cousin Rachel ten year ago , '' say Cecily , `` and ask her if she might open the chest to see if the moth have get into it .
There 's a crack in the back as big a your finger .
Cousin Rachel write back that if it be n't for one thing that be in the trunk she would ask mother to open the chest and dispose of the thing a she like .
But she could not bear that any one but herself should see or touch that one thing .
So she want it leave a it be .
Ma say she wash her hand of it , moth or no moth .
She say if Cousin Rachel have to move that chest every time the floor have to be scrub it would cure her of her sentimental nonsense .
But I think , '' conclude Cecily , `` that I would feel just like Cousin Rachel in her place . ''
`` What be the thing she could n't bear any one to see ? ''
I ask .
`` Ma think it be her wed dress .
But father say he believe it be Will Montague 's picture , '' say Felicity .
`` He saw her put it in .
Father know some of the thing that be in the chest .
He be ten year old , and he saw her pack it .
There 's a white muslin wedding dress and a veil -- and -- and -- a -- a '' -- Felicity drop her eye and blush painfully .
`` A petticoat , embroider by hand from hem to belt , '' say the Story Girl calmly .
`` And a china fruit basket with an apple on the handle , '' go on Felicity , much relieve .
`` And a tea set , and a blue candle-stick . ''
`` I 'd dearly love to see all the thing that be in it , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Pa say it must never be open without Cousin Rachel 's permission , '' say Cecily .
Felix and I look at the chest reverently .
It have take on a new significance in our eye , and seem like a tomb wherein lay bury some dead romance of the vanished year .
`` What happen to Will Montague ? ''
I ask .
`` Nothing ! ''
say the Story Girl viciously .
`` He just go on living and flourishing .
He patch up matter with his creditor after awhile , and come back to the Island ; and in the end he marry a real nice girl , with money , and be very happy .
Did you ever HEAR of anything so unjust ? ''
`` Beverley King , '' suddenly cry Felicity , who have be peer into a pot , `` YOU 'VE GONE AND PUT THE TURNIPS ON TO BOIL WHOLE JUST LIKE POTATOES ! ''
`` Was n't that right ? ''
I cry , in an agony of shame .
`` Right ! ''
but Felicity have already whisk the turnip out , and be slice them , while all the others be laugh at me .
I have add a tradition on my own account to the family archive .
Uncle Roger roar when he hear it ; and he roar again at night over Peter 's account of Felix attempt to milk a cow .
Felix have previously acquire the knack of extract milk from the udder .
But he have never before try to `` milk a whole cow . ''
He do not get on well ; the cow tramp on his foot , and finally upset the bucket .
`` What be you to do when a cow wo n't stand straight ? ''
splutter Felix angrily .
`` That 's the question , '' say Uncle Roger , shake his head gravely .
Uncle Roger 's laughter be hard to bear , but his gravity be hard .
Meanwhile , in the pantry the Story Girl , apron-enshrouded , be be initiate into the mystery of bread-making .
Under Felicity 's eye she set the bread , and on the morrow she be to bake it .
`` The first thing you must do in the morning be knead it well , '' say Felicity , `` and the early it 's do the good -- because it 's such a warm night . ''
With that we go to bed , and sleep as soundly a if tragedy of blue chest and turnip and crooked cow have no place in the scheme of thing at all .
CHAPTER XIII .
AN OLD PROVERB WITH A NEW MEANING It be half-past five when we boys get up the next morning .
We be join on the stair by Felicity , yawn and rosy .
`` Oh , dear me , I oversleep myself .
Uncle Roger want breakfast at six .
Well , I suppose the fire be on anyhow , for the Story Girl be up .
I guess she get up early to knead the bread .
She could n't sleep all night for worry over it . ''
The fire be on , and a flushed and triumphant Story Girl be take a loaf of bread from the oven .
`` Just look , '' she say proudly .
`` I have every bit of the bread bake .
I get up at three , and it be lovely and light , so I just give it a right good kneading and pop it into the oven .
And it 's all do and out of the way .
But the loaf do n't seem quite as big a they should be , '' she add doubtfully .
`` Sara Stanley ! ''
Felicity fly across the kitchen .
`` Do you mean that you put the bread right into the oven after you knead it without leave it to rise a second time ? ''
The Story Girl turn quite pale .
`` Yes , I do , '' she falter .
`` Oh , Felicity , be n't it right ? ''
`` You 've ruin the bread , '' say Felicity flatly .
`` It 's as heavy a a stone .
I declare , Sara Stanley , I 'd rather have a little common sense than be a great story teller . ''
Bitter indeed be the poor Story Girl 's mortification .
`` Do n't tell Uncle Roger , '' she implore humbly .
`` Oh , I wo n't tell him , '' promise Felicity amiably .
`` It 's lucky there 's enough old bread to do to-day .
This will go to the hen .
But it 's an awful waste of good flour . ''
The Story Girl creep out with Felix and me to the morning orchard , while Dan and Peter go to do the barn work .
`` It be n't ANY use for me to try to learn to cook , '' she say .
`` Never mind , '' I say consolingly .
`` You can tell splendid story . ''
`` But what good would that do a hungry boy ? ''
wail the Story Girl .
`` Boys ai n't ALWAYS hungry , '' say Felix gravely .
`` There 's time when they ai n't . ''
`` I do n't believe it , '' say the Story Girl drearily .
`` Besides , '' add Felix in the tone of one who say while there be life there be yet hope , `` you may learn to cook yet if you keep on try . ''
`` But Aunt Olivia wo n't let me waste the stuff .
My only hope be to learn this week .
But I suppose Felicity be so disgusted with me now that she wo n't give me any more lesson . ''
`` I do n't care , '' say Felix .
`` I like you good than Felicity , even if you ca n't cook .
There 's lot of folk can make bread .
But there be n't many who can tell a story like you . ''
`` But it 's good to be useful than just interesting , '' sigh the Story Girl bitterly .
And Felicity , who be useful , would , in her secret soul , have give anything to be interesting .
Which be the way of human nature .
Company descend on u that afternoon .
First come Aunt Janet 's sister , Mrs. Patterson , with a daughter of sixteen year and a son of two .
They be follow by a buggy-load of Markdale people ; and finally , Mrs. Elder Frewen and her sister from Vancouver , with two small daughter of the latter , arrive .
`` It never rain but it pour , '' say Uncle Roger , a he go out to take their horse .
But Felicity 's foot be on her native heath .
She have be bake all the afternoon , and , with a pantry well stock with biscuit , cooky , cake , and pie , she care not if all Carlisle come to tea .
Cecily set the table , and the Story Girl wait on it and wash all the dish afterwards .
But all the blushing honour fell to Felicity , who receive so many compliment that her air be quite unbearable for the rest of the week .
She preside at the head of the table with as much grace and dignity a if she have be five time twelve year old , and seem to know by instinct just who take sugar and who take it not .
She be flush with excitement and pleasure , and be so pretty that I could hardly eat for look at her -- which be the high compliment in a boy 's power to pay .
The Story Girl , on the contrary , be under eclipse .
She be pale and lustreless from her disturbed night and early rising ; and no opportunity offer to tell a melting tale .
Nobody take any notice of her .
It be Felicity 's day .
After tea Mrs. Frewen and her sister wish to visit their father 's grave in the Carlisle churchyard .
It appear that everybody want to go with them ; but it be evident that somebody must stay home with Jimmy Patterson , who have just fall sound asleep on the kitchen sofa .
Dan finally volunteer to look after him .
He have a new Henty book which he want to finish , and that , he say , be well fun than a walk to the graveyard .
`` I think we 'll be back before he wake , '' say Mrs. Patterson , `` and anyhow he be very good and wo n't be any trouble .
Do n't let him go outside , though .
He have a cold now . ''
We go away , leave Dan sit on the door-sill read his book , and Jimmy P. snooze blissfully on the sofa .
When we return -- Felix and the girl and I be ahead of the others -- Dan be still sit in precisely the same place and attitude ; but there be no Jimmy in sight .
`` Dan , where 's the baby ? ''
cry Felicity .
Dan look around .
His jaw fell in blank amazement .
I never say any one look as foolish a Dan at that moment .
`` Good gracious , I do n't know , '' he say helplessly .
`` You 've be so deep in that wretched book that he 's get out , and dear know where he be , '' cry Felicity distractedly .
`` I be n't , '' cry Dan .
`` He MUST be in the house .
I 've be sit right across the door ever since you leave , and he could n't have get out unless he crawl right over me .
He must be in the house . ''
`` He be n't in the kitchen , '' say Felicity rush about wildly , `` and he could n't get into the other part of the house , for I shut the hall door tight , and no baby could open it -- and it 's shut tight yet .
So be all the window .
He MUST have go out of that door , Dan King , and it 's your fault . ''
`` He DID N'T go out of this door , '' reiterate Dan stubbornly .
`` I know that . ''
`` Well , where be he , then ?
He be n't here .
Did he melt into air ? ''
demand Felicity .
`` Oh , come and look for him , all of you .
Do n't stand round like ninny .
We MUST find him before his mother get here .
Dan King , you 're an idiot ! ''
Dan be too frighten to resent this , at the time .
However and wherever Jimmy have go , he WAS go , so much be certain .
We tear about the house and yard like maniac ; we look into every likely and unlikely place .
But Jimmy we could not find , anymore than if he have indeed melt into air .
Mrs. Patterson come , and we have not find him .
Things be get serious .
Uncle Roger and Peter be summon from the field .
Mrs. Patterson become hysterical , and be take into the spare room with such remedy a could be suggest .
Everybody blame poor Dan .
Cecily ask him what he would feel like if Jimmy be never , never find .
The Story Girl have a gruesome recollection of some baby at Markdale who have wander away like that -- `` And they never find him till the next spring , and all they find be -- HIS SKELETON , with the grass grow through it , '' she whisper .
`` This beat me , '' say Uncle Roger , when a fruitless hour have elapse .
`` I do hope that baby have n't wander down to the swamp .
It seem impossible he could walk so far ; but I must go and see .
Felicity , hand me my high boot out from under the sofa , there 's a girl . ''
Felicity , pale and tearful , drop on her knee and lift the cretonne frill of the sofa .
There , his head pillow hardly on Uncle Roger 's boot , lay Jimmy Patterson , still sound asleep !
`` Well , I 'll be -- jiggered ! ''
say Uncle Roger .
`` I KNEW he never go out of the door , '' cry Dan triumphantly .
When the last buggy have drive away , Felicity set a batch of bread , and the rest of u sit around the back porch step in the cat 's light and ate cherry , shoot the stone at each other .
Cecily be in quest of information .
`` What do ` it never rain but it pour ' mean ? ''
`` Oh , it mean if anything happen something else be sure to happen , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I 'll illustrate .
There 's Mrs. Murphy .
She never have a proposal in her life till she be forty , and then she have three in the one week , and she be so flustered she take the wrong one and have be sorry ever since .
Do you see what it mean now ? ''
`` Yes , I guess so , '' say Cecily somewhat doubtfully .
Later on we hear her impart her newly acquire knowledge to Felicity in the pantry . ''
` It never rain but it pour ' mean that nobody want to marry you for ever so long , and then lot of people do . ''
CHAPTER XIV .
FORBIDDEN FRUIT We be all , with the exception of Uncle Roger , more or less grumpy in the household of King next day .
Perhaps our nerve have be upset by the excitement attendant on Jimmy Patterson 's disappearance .
But it be more likely that our crankiness be the result of the supper we have eat the previous night .
Even child can not devour mince pie , and cold fry pork ham , and fruit cake before go to bed with entire impunity .
Aunt Janet have forget to warn Uncle Roger to keep an eye on our bedtime snack , and we eat what seem good unto u .
Some of u have frightful dream , and all of u carry chip on our shoulder at breakfast .
Felicity and Dan begin a bickering which they keep up the entire day .
Felicity have a natural aptitude for what we call `` bossing , '' and in her mother 's absence she deem that she have a right to rule supreme .
She know good than to make any attempt to assert authority over the Story Girl , and Felix and I be allow some length of tether ; but Cecily , Dan , and Peter be expect to submit dutifully to her decree .
In the main they do ; but on this particular morning Dan be plainly inclined to rebel .
He have have time to grow sore over the thing that Felicity have say to him when Jimmy Patterson be think lost , and he begin the day with a flatly express determination that he be not go to let Felicity rule the roost .
It be not a pleasant day , and to make matter bad it rain until late in the afternoon .
The Story Girl have not recover from the mortification of the previous day ; she would not talk , and she would not tell a single story ; she sit on Rachel Ward 's chest and eat her breakfast with the air of a martyr .
After breakfast she wash the dish and do the bed-room work in grim silence ; then , with a book under one arm and Pat under the other , she betook herself to the window-seat in the upstairs hall , and would not be lure from that retreat , charm we never so wisely .
She stroke the purring Paddy , and read steadily on , with madden indifference to all our pleading .
Even Cecily , the meek and mild , be snappish , and complain of headache .
Peter have go home to see his mother , and Uncle Roger have go to Markdale on business .
Sara Ray come up , but be so snub by Felicity that she go home , cry .
Felicity get the dinner by herself , disdain to ask or command assistance .
She bang thing about and rattle the stove cover until even Cecily protest from her sofa .
Dan sit on the floor and whittle , his sole aim and object be to make a mess and annoy Felicity , in which noble ambition he succeed perfectly .
`` I wish Aunt Janet and Uncle Alec be home , '' say Felix .
`` It 's not half so much fun have the grown-ups away a I think it would be . ''
`` I wish I be back in Toronto , '' I say sulkily .
The mince pie be to blame for THAT wish .
`` I wish you be , I 'm sure , '' say Felicity , riddle the fire noisily .
`` Any one who live with you , Felicity King , will always be wish he be somewhere else , '' say Dan .
`` I be n't talk to you , Dan King , '' retort Felicity , '' ` Speak when you 're speak to , come when you 're call . ' ''
`` Oh , oh , oh , '' wail Cecily on the sofa .
`` I WISH it would stop raining .
I WISH my head would stop aching .
I WISH ma have never go away .
I WISH you 'd leave Felicity alone , Dan . ''
`` I wish girl have some sense , '' say Dan -- which bring the orgy of wish to an end for the time .
A wishing fairy might have have the time of her life in the King kitchen that morning -- particularly if she be a cynically inclined fairy .
But even the effect of unholy snack wear away at length .
By tea-time thing have brighten up .
The rain have cease , and the old , low-raftered room be full of sunshine which dance on the shin dish of the dresser , make mosaic on the floor , and flicker over the table whereon a delicious meal be spread .
Felicity have put on her blue muslin , and look so beautiful in it that her good humour be quite restore .
Cecily 's headache be good , and the Story Girl , refresh by an afternoon siesta , come down with smile and sparkle eye .
Dan alone continue to nurse his grievance , and would not even laugh when the Story Girl tell u a tale brought to mind by some of the `` Rev . Mr. Scott 's plum '' which be on the table .
`` The Rev . Mr. Scott be the man who think the pulpit door must be make for speerits , you know , '' she say .
`` I hear Uncle Edward tell ever so many story about him .
He be call to this congregation , and he labour here long and faithfully , and be much beloved , though he be very eccentric . ''
`` What do that mean ? ''
ask Peter .
`` Hush !
It just mean queer , '' say Cecily , nudge him with her elbow .
`` A common man would be queer , but when it 's a minister , it 's eccentric . ''
`` When he get very old , '' continue the Story Girl , `` the Presbytery think it be time he be retire .
HE do n't think so ; but the Presbytery have their way , because there be so many of them to one of him .
He be retire , and a young man be call to Carlisle .
Mr. Scott go to live in town , but he come out to Carlisle very often , and visit all the people regularly , just the same a when he be their minister .
The young minister be a very good young man , and try to do his duty ; but he be dreadfully afraid of meet old Mr. Scott , because he have be tell that the old minister be very angry at be set aside , and would likely give him a sound drubbing , if he ever meet him .
One day the young minister be visit the Crawfords in Markdale , when they suddenly hear old Mr. Scott 's voice in the kitchen .
The young minister turn pale a the dead , and implore Mrs. Crawford to hide him .
But she could n't get him out of the room , and all she could do be to hide him in the china closet .
The young minister slip into the china closet , and old Mr. Scott come into the room .
He talk very nicely , and read , and prayed .
They make very long prayer in those day , you know ; and at the end of his prayer he say , ` Oh Lord , bless the poor young man hiding in the closet .
Give him courage not to fear the face of man .
Make him a burning and a shin light to this sadly abused congregation . '
Just imagine the feeling of the young minister in the china closet !
But he come right out like a man , though his face be very red , as soon a Mr. Scott have do praying .
And Mr. Scott be lovely to him , and shake hand , and never mention the china closet .
And they be the best of friend ever afterwards . ''
`` How do old Mr. Scott find out the young minister be in the closet ? ''
ask Felix .
`` Nobody ever know .
They suppose he have see him through the window before he come into the house , and guess he must be in the closet -- because there be no way for him to get out of the room . ''
`` Mr. Scott plant the yellow plum tree in Grandfather 's time , '' say Cecily , peel one of the plum , `` and when he do it he say it be a Christian an act a he ever do .
I wonder what he mean .
I do n't see anything very Christian about plant a tree . ''
`` I do , '' say the Story Girl sagely .
When next we assemble ourselves together , it be after milking , and the care of the day be do with .
We foregather in the balsam-fragrant aisle of the fir wood , and eat early August apple to such an extent that the Story Girl say we make her think of the Irishman 's pig .
`` An Irishman who live at Markdale have a little pig , '' she say , `` and he give it a pailful of mush .
The pig at the whole pailful , and then the Irishman put the pig IN the pail , and it do n't fill more than half the pail .
Now , how be that , when it hold a whole pailful of mush ? ''
This seem to be a rather unanswerable kind of conundrum .
We discuss the problem a we roam the wood , and Dan and Peter almost quarrel over it , Dan maintain that the thing be impossible , and Peter be of the opinion that the mush be somehow `` make thicker '' in the process of be eat , and so take up less room .
During the discussion we come out to the fence of the hill pasture where grow the `` bad berry '' bush .
Just what these `` bad berry '' be I can not tell .
We never know their real name .
They be small , red-clustered berry of a glossy , seductive appearance , and we be forbid to eat them , because it be think they might be poisonous .
Dan pick a cluster and hold it up .
`` Dan King , do n't you DARE eat those berry , '' say Felicity in her `` bossy '' tone .
`` They 're poison .
Drop them right away . ''
Now , Dan have not have the slight intention of eat the berry .
But at Felicity 's prohibition the rebellion which have smoulder in him all day break into sudden flame .
He would show her !
`` I 'll eat them if I please , Felicity King , '' he say in a fury : `` I do n't believe they 're poison .
Look here ! ''
Dan cram the whole bunch into his capacious mouth and chew it up .
`` They taste great , '' he say , smack ; and he eat two more cluster , regardless of our horror-stricken protestation and Felicity 's pleading .
We fear that Dan would drop dead on the spot .
But nothing occur immediately .
When an hour have pass we conclude that the bad berry be not poison after all , and we look upon Dan a quite a hero for dare to eat them .
`` I know they would n't hurt me , '' he say loftily .
`` Felicity 's so fond of make a fuss over everything . ''
Nevertheless , when it grow dark and we return to the house , I notice that Dan be rather pale and quiet .
He lay down on the kitchen sofa .
`` Do n't you feel all right , Dan ? ''
I whisper anxiously .
`` Shut up , '' he say .
I shut up .
Felicity and Cecily be set out a lunch in the pantry when we be all startle by a loud groan from the sofa .
`` Oh , I 'm sick -- I 'm awful sick , '' say Dan abjectly , all the defiance and bravado go out of him .
We all go to piece , except Cecily , who alone retain her presence of mind .
`` Have you get a pain in your stomach ? ''
she demand .
`` I 've get an awful pain here , if that 's where my stomach be , '' moan Dan , put his hand on a portion of his anatomy considerably below his stomach .
`` Oh -- oh -- oh ! ''
`` Go for Uncle Roger , '' command Cecily , pale but compose .
`` Felicity , put on the kettle .
Dan , I 'm go to give you mustard and warm water . ''
The mustard and warm water produce it proper effect promptly , but give Dan no relief .
He continue to writhe and groan .
Uncle Roger , who have be summon from his own place , go at once for the doctor , tell Peter to go down the hill for Mrs. Ray .
Peter go , but return accompany by Sara only .
Mrs. Ray and Judy Pineau be both away .
Sara might well have stay home ; she be of no use , and could only add to the general confusion , wander aimlessly about , cry and ask if Dan be go to die .
Cecily take charge of thing .
Felicity might charm the palate , and the Story Girl bind captive the soul ; but when pain and sickness wring the brow it be Cecily who be the ministering angel .
She make the writhing Dan go to bed .
She make him swallow every available antidote which be recommend in `` the doctor 's book ; '' and she apply hot cloth to him until her faithful little hand be half scald off .
There be no doubt Dan be suffer intense pain .
He moan and writhe , and cry for his mother .
`` Oh , be n't it dreadful ! ''
say Felicity , wring her hand a she walk the kitchen floor .
`` Oh , why do n't the doctor come ?
I TOLD Dan the bad berry be poison .
But surely they ca n't kill people ALTOGETHER . ''
`` Pa 's cousin die of eat something forty year ago , '' sob Sara Ray .
`` Hold your tongue , '' say Peter in a fierce whisper .
`` You oughter have more sense than to say such thing to the girl .
They do n't want to be any bad scar than they be . ''
`` But Pa 's cousin DID die , '' reiterate Sara .
`` My Aunt Jane use to rub whisky on for a pain , '' suggest Peter .
`` We have n't any whisky , '' say Felicity disapprovingly .
`` This be a temperance house . ''
`` But rub whisky on the OUTSIDE be n't any harm , '' argue Peter .
`` It 's only when you take it inside it be bad for you . ''
`` Well , we have n't any , anyhow , '' say Felicity .
`` I suppose blueberry wine would n't do in it place ? ''
Peter do not think blueberry wine would be any good .
It be ten o'clock before Dan begin to get well ; but from that time he improve rapidly .
When the doctor , who have be away from home when Uncle Roger reach Markdale , come at half past ten , he find his patient very weak and white , but free from pain .
Dr. Grier pat Cecily on the head , tell her she be a little brick , and have do just the right thing , examine some of the fatal berry and give it a his opinion that they be probably poisonous , administer some powder to Dan and advise him not to tamper with forbidden fruit in future , and go away .
Mrs. Ray now appear , look for Sara , and say she would stay all night with u .
`` I 'll be much oblige to you if you will , '' say Uncle Roger .
`` I feel a bit shook .

If anything have happen I could never have forgive myself -- though I believe it 's beyond the power of mortal man to keep watch over the thing child WILL eat .
Now , you young fry , get straight off to your bed .
Dan be out of danger , and you ca n't do any more good .
Not that any of you have do much , except Cecily .
She 's get a head of her shoulder . ''
`` It 's be a horrid day all through , '' say Felicity drearily , a we climb the stair .
`` I suppose we make it horrid ourselves , '' say the Story Girl candidly .
`` But it 'll be a good story to tell sometime , '' she add .
`` I 'm awful tired and thankful , '' sigh Cecily .
We all felt that way .
CHAPTER XV .
A DISOBEDIENT BROTHER Dan be his own man again in the morning , though rather pale and weak ; he want to get up , but Cecily order him to stay in bed .
Fortunately Felicity forget to repeat the command , so Dan do stay in bed .
Cecily carry his meal to him , and read a Henty book to him all her spare time .
The Story Girl go up and tell him wondrous tale ; and Sara Ray bring him a pudding she have make herself .
Sara 's intention be good , but the pudding -- well , Dan feed most of it to Paddy , who have curl himself up at the foot of the bed , give the world assurance of a cat by his mellifluous purring .
`` Ai n't he just a great old fellow ? ''
say Dan .
`` He know I 'm kind of sick , just as well a a human .
He never pay no attention to me when I 'm well . ''

In August it be a place of shady sweetness , fragrant with the odour of ripen apple , full of dear , delicate shadow .
Through it opening we look afar to the blue rim of the hill and over green , old , tranquil field , lie the sunset glow .
Overhead the lacing leave make a green , murmurous roof .
There be no such thing a hurry in the world , while we linger there and talk of `` cabbage and king . ''
A tale of the Story Girl 's , wherein prince be thick than blackberry , and queen as common a buttercup , lead to our discussion of king .
We wonder what it would be like to be a king .

`` Maybe they use to once , but now they wear hat .

There be n't one in this country anywhere .
Perhaps I 'll get a glimpse of some when I go to Europe . ''
Well , the Story Girl be destine to stand before king herself , and she be to be one whom they delight to honour .

`` It 's so expressive .
Squ-u-e-l-ch ! ''
Certainly it be a lovely word , a the Story Girl say it .
Even a king would not have mind be squelch , if it be do to music like that .

`` He say Martin ca n't call his soul his own since he be marry . ''
`` I 'm glad of it , '' say Cecily vindictively .
We all star .
This be so very unlike Cecily .

Would YOU forgive James Forbes if he have call YOU Johnny ? ''

If you could have hear the Story Girl 's `` bur-r-r-r ! ''

Twas the McCloskeys and the devil . ' ''

Twas the McCloskeys and the Old Scratch , ' '' say the Story Girl reflectively , a if she be try to see which version be the more effective .

`` Not long after he be marry his wife be n't quite ready for church one morning when it be time to go .

We sit still and count the hundred .

`` What on earth be you young fry do up at this time of night ? ''

`` Felicity King , if you do n't watch out you 'll grow up into the sort of woman who drive her husband to drink , '' say Uncle Roger gravely .
`` How could I tell Dan would act so like a mule ! ''

That last question be the most unkind cut of all .

She confide to me a we climb the stair that she hat Uncle Roger .
Her red lip quiver and the tear of wounded pride brim over in her beautiful blue eye .

`` He 's only a grown-up . ''
CHAPTER XVI .
THE GHOSTLY BELL Friday be a comfortable day in the household of King .
Everybody be in good humour .
The Story Girl sparkle through several tale that range from the afrites and jinns of Eastern myth , through the piping day of chivalry , down to the homely anecdote of Carlisle workaday folk .
She be in turn an Oriental princess behind a silken veil , the bride who follow her bridegroom to the war of Palestine disguise a a page , the gallant lady who ransom her diamond necklace by dance a coranto with a highwayman on a moonlit heath , and `` Buskirk 's girl '' who join the Sons and Daughters of Temperance `` just to see what be into it ; '' and in each impersonation she be so thoroughly the thing impersonate that it be a matter of surprise to u when she emerge from each our own familiar Story Girl again .
Cecily and Sara Ray find a `` sweet '' new knit lace pattern in an old magazine and spend a happy afternoon learn it and `` talk secret . ''
Chancing -- accidentally , I vow -- to overhear certain of these secret , I learn that Sara Ray have name an apple for Johnny Price -- `` and , Cecily , true 's you live , there be eight seed in it , and you know eight mean ` they both love ' '' -- while Cecily admit that Willy Fraser have write on his slate and show it to her , `` If you love me a I love you , No knife can cut our love in two '' -- `` but , Sara Ray , NEVER you breathe this to a living soul . ''
Felix also aver that he hear Sara ask Cecily very seriously , `` Cecily , how old must we be before we can have a REAL beau ? ''
But Sara always deny it ; so I be inclined to believe Felix simply make it up himself .
Paddy distinguish himself by catch a rat , and be intolerably conceited about it -- until Sara Ray cure him by call him a `` dear , sweet cat , '' and kiss him between the ear .
Then Pat sneak abjectly off , his tail drooping .
He resent be call a sweet cat .
He have a sense of humour , have Pat .
Very few cat have ; and most of them have such an inordinate appetite for flattery that they will swallow any amount of it and thrive thereon .
Paddy have a finer taste .
The Story Girl and I be the only one who could pay him compliment to his liking .
The Story Girl would box his ear with her fist and say , `` Bless your gray heart , Paddy , you 're a good sort of old rascal , '' and Pat would purr his satisfaction ; I use to take a handful of the skin on his back , shake him gently and say , `` Pat , you 've forget more than any human be ever know , '' and I vow Paddy would lick his chop with delight .
But to be call `` a sweet cat ! ''
Oh , Sara , Sara !
Felicity try -- and have the most gratifying luck with -- a new and complicated cake recipe -- a gorgeous compound of a plumminess to make your mouth water .
The number of egg she use in it would have shock Aunt Janet 's thrifty soul , but that cake , like beauty , be it own excuse .
Uncle Roger eat three slice of it at tea-time and tell Felicity she be an artist .
The poor man mean it a a compliment ; but Felicity , who know Uncle Blair be an artist and have a poor opinion of such fry , look indignant and retort , indeed she be n't !
`` Peter say there 's any amount of raspberry back in the maple clearing , '' say Dan .

You boys good go alone . ''
`` Peter and I will attend to the milking for one evening , '' say Uncle Roger .
`` You can all go .
I have an idea that a raspberry pie for to-morrow night , when the folk come home , would hit the right spot . ''
Accordingly , after tea we all set off , arm with jug and cup .
Felicity , thoughtful creature , also take a small basketful of jelly cooky along with her .
We have to go back through the maple wood to the extreme end of Uncle Roger 's farm -- a pretty walk , through a world of green , whisper bough and spice-sweet fern , and shift patch of sunlight .
The raspberry be plentiful , and we be not long in fill our receptacle .
Then we foregather around a tiny wood spring , cold and pellucid under it young maple , and eat the jelly cooky ; and the Story Girl tell u a tale of a haunted spring in a mountain glen where a fair white lady dwelt , who pledge all comer in a golden cup with jewel bright .
`` And if you drink of the cup with her , '' say the Story Girl , her eye glow through the emerald dusk about u , `` you be never see in the world again ; you be whisk straightway to fairyland , and live there with a fairy bride .
And you never WANTED to come back to earth , because when you drink of the magic cup you forget all your past life , except for one day in every year when you be allow to remember it . ''
`` I wish there be such a place a fairyland -- and a way to get to it , '' say Cecily .
`` I think there IS such a place -- in spite of Uncle Edward , '' say the Story Girl dreamily , `` and I think there be a way of get there too , if we could only find it . ''
Well , the Story Girl be right .
There be such a place a fairyland -- but only child can find the way to it .
And they do not know that it be fairyland until they have grow so old that they forget the way .
One bitter day , when they seek it and can not find it , they realize what they have lose ; and that be the tragedy of life .
On that day the gate of Eden be shut behind them and the age of gold be over .
Henceforth they must dwell in the common light of common day .
Only a few , who remain child at heart , can ever find that fair , lose path again ; and bless be they above mortal .
They , and only they , can bring u tidings from that dear country where we once sojourn and from which we must evermore be exile .
The world call them it singer and poet and artist and story-tellers ; but they be just people who have never forget the way to fairyland .
As we sit there the Awkward Man pass by , with his gun over his shoulder and his dog at his side .
He do not look like an awkward man , there in the heart of the maple wood .
He stride along right masterfully and lift his head with the air of one who be monarch of all he survey .
The Story Girl kiss her fingertip to him with the delightful audacity which be a part of her ; and the Awkward Man pluck off his hat and sweep her a stately and graceful bow .
`` I do n't understand why they call him the awkward man , '' say Cecily , when he be out of earshot .
`` You 'd understand why if you ever saw him at a party or a picnic , '' say Felicity , `` try to pass plate and drop them whenever a woman look at him .
They say it 's pitiful to see him . ''
`` I must get well acquaint with that man next summer , '' say the Story Girl .
`` If I put it off any long it will be too late .
I 'm grow so fast , Aunt Olivia say I 'll have to wear ankle skirt next summer .
If I begin to look grown-up he 'll get frighten of me , and then I 'll never find out the Golden Milestone mystery . ''
`` Do you think he 'll ever tell you who Alice be ? ''
I ask .
`` I have a notion who Alice be already , '' say the mysterious creature .
But she would tell u nothing more .
When the jelly cooky be all eat it be high time to be move homeward , for when the dark come down there be more comfortable place than a rustle maple wood and the precinct of a possibly enchant spring .
When we reach the foot of the orchard and enter it through a gap in the hedge it be the magical , mystical time of `` between light . ''
Off to the west be a daffodil glow hanging over the valley of lose sunset , and Grandfather King 's huge willow rise up against it like a rounded mountain of foliage .
In the east , above the maple wood , be a silvery sheen that hint the moonrise .
But the orchard be a place of shadow and mysterious sound .
Midway up the open space in it heart we meet Peter ; and if ever a boy be give over to sheer terror that boy be Peter .
His face be as white a a sunburned face could be , and his eye be brim with panic .
`` Peter , what be the matter ? ''

Not the Story Girl herself could have invest that `` something '' with more of creepy horror .
We all draw close together .
I felt a crinkly feeling along my back which I have never know before .

`` Nonsense ! ''

`` There be n't a bell in the house to ring .
You must have imagine it , Peter .
Or else Uncle Roger be try to fool u . ''

You would n't catch any of u do it .
We be almost a badly scar a Peter .
There we stand in a huddled demoralize group .
Oh , what an eerie place that orchard be !
What shadow !
What noise !
What spooky swoop of bat !
You COULD N'T look every way at once , and goodness only know what might be behind you !
`` There CA N'T be anybody in the house , '' say Felicity .
`` Well , here 's the key -- go and see for yourself , '' say Peter .
Felicity have no intention of go and see .
`` I think you boys ought to go , '' she say , retreat behind the defence of sex .
`` You ought to be braver than girl . ''
`` But we ai n't , '' say Felix candidly .
`` I would n't be much scar of anything REAL .
But a haunt house be a different thing . ''
`` I always think something have to be do in a place before it could be haunt , '' say Cecily .
`` Somebody kill or something like that , you know .
Nothing like that ever happen in our family .
The Kings have always be respectable . ''
`` Perhaps it be Emily King 's ghost , '' whisper Felix .
`` She never appear anywhere but in the orchard , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Oh , oh , child , be n't there something under Uncle Alec 's tree ? ''
We peer fearfully through the gloom .
There WAS something -- something that waver and flutter -- advanced -- retreat -- `` That 's only my old apron , '' say Felicity .
`` I hang it there to-day when I be look for the white hen 's nest .
Oh , what shall we do ?
Uncle Roger may not be back for hour .
I CA N'T believe there 's anything in the house . ''
`` Maybe it 's only Peg Bowen , '' suggest Dan .
There be not a great deal of comfort in this .
We be almost as much afraid of Peg Bowen a we would be of any spectral visitant .
Peter scoff at the idea .
`` Peg Bowen be n't in the house before your Uncle Roger lock it up , and how could she get in afterwards ? ''
he say .
`` No , it be n't Peg Bowen .
It 's SOMETHING that WALKS . ''
`` I know a story about a ghost , '' say the Story Girl , the ruling passion strong even in extremity .
`` It be about a ghost with eyehole but no eye -- '' `` Do n't , '' cry Cecily hysterically .
`` Do n't you go on !
Do n't you say another word !
I ca n't bear it !
Do n't you ! ''
The Story Girl do n't .
But she have say enough .
There be something in the quality of a ghost with eyehole but no eye that freeze our young blood .
There never be in all the world six more badly scar child than those who huddle in the old King orchard that August night .
All at once -- something -- leap from the bough of a tree and alight before u .
We split the air with a simultaneous shriek .

But there be n't -- all around u be only those shadowy arcade .
Then we saw with shame that it be only our Paddy .
`` Pat , Pat , '' I say , pick him up , feel a certain comfort in his soft , solid body .

But Pat would none of u .
He struggle out of my clasp and disappear over the long grass with soundless leap .
He be no longer our tame , domestic , well acquaint Paddy .
He be a strange , furtive animal -- a `` questing beast . ''

The shadow have be still before ; now they move and dance , a the night wind toss the bough .
The old house , with it dreadful secret , be white and clear against the dark background of spruce .
We be woefully tire , but we could not sit down because the grass be reek with dew .
`` The Family Ghost only appear in daylight , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I would n't mind see a ghost in daylight .
But after dark be another thing . ''

Oh , how I wish I could believe it !
`` Then what ring that bell ? ''
say Peter .
`` Bells do n't ring of themselves , I s ` pose , specially when there ai n't any in the house to ring . ''
`` Oh , will Uncle Roger never come home ! ''
sobbed Felicity .
`` I know he 'll laugh at u awful , but it 's good to be laugh at than scared like this . ''

Never be there a more welcome sound than the rumble of his wheel in the lane .
We run to the orchard gate and swarm across the yard , just a Uncle Roger alight at the front door .
He star at u in the moonlight .
`` Have you torment any one into eat more bad berry , Felicity ? ''

Peter hear it .
Do n't go in . ''

`` I 've give up try to fathom you young one .
Peter , where 's the key ?
What yarn have you be tell ? ''

Uncle Roger unlock and flung open the front door .
As he do so , clear and sweet , ring out ten bell-like chime .
