`` There 's the bell ! ''
We have to wait until Uncle Roger stop laugh before we hear the explanation .
We think he never WOULD stop .
`` That 's Grandfather King 's old clock striking , '' he say , as soon a he be able to speak .
`` Sammy Prott come along after tea , when you be away to the forge , Peter , and I give him permission to clean the old clock .
He have it go merrily in no time .
And now it have almost frighten you poor little monkey to death . ''
We hear Uncle Roger chuckle all the way to the barn .
`` Uncle Roger can laugh , '' say Cecily , with a quiver in her voice , `` but it 's no laughing matter to be so scared .
I just feel sick , I be so frightened . ''
`` I would n't mind if he 'd laugh once and have it do with it , '' say Felicity bitterly .
`` But he 'll laugh at u for a year , and tell the story to every soul that come to the place . ''
`` You ca n't blame him for that , '' say the Story Girl .
`` I shall tell it , too .
I do n't care if the joke be as much on myself a any one .
A story be a story , no matter who it 's on .
But it IS hateful to be laugh at -- and grown-ups always do it .
I never will when I 'm grown up .
I 'll remember good . ''
`` It 's all Peter 's fault , '' say Felicity .
`` I do think he might have have more sense than to take a clock strike for a bell ringing . ''
`` I never hear that kind of a strike before , '' protest Peter .
`` It do n't sound a bit like other clock .
And the door be shut and the sound kind o ' muffle .
It 's all very fine to say you would have know what it be , but I do n't believe you would . ''
`` I would n't have , '' say the Story Girl honestly .
`` I think it WAS a bell when I hear it , and the door open , too .
Let u be fair , Felicity . ''
`` I 'm dreadful tired , '' sigh Cecily .
We be all `` dreadful tired , '' for this be the third night of late hour and nerve rack strain .
But it be over two hour since we have eat the cooky , and Felicity suggest that a saucerful apiece of raspberry and cream would not be hard to take .
It be not , for any one but Cecily , who could n't swallow a mouthful .
`` I 'm glad father and mother will be back to-morrow night , '' she say .
`` It 's too exciting when they 're away .
That 's my opinion . ''
CHAPTER XVII .
THE PROOF OF THE PUDDING Felicity be cumber with many care the next morning .
For one thing , the whole house must be put in apple pie order ; and for another , an elaborate supper must be prepare for the expected return of the traveller that night .
Felicity devote her whole attention to this , and leave the secondary preparation of the regular meal to Cecily and the Story Girl .
It be agree that the latter be to make a cornmeal pudding for dinner .
In spite of her disaster with the bread , the Story Girl have be take cook lesson from Felicity all the week , and get on tolerably well , although , mindful of her former mistake , she never venture on anything without Felicity 's approval .
But Felicity have no time to oversee her this morning .
`` You must attend to the pudding yourself , '' she say .
`` The recipe 's so plain and simple even you ca n't go astray , and if there 's anything you do n't understand you can ask me .
But do n't bother me if you can help it . ''
The Story Girl do not bother her once .
The pudding be concoct and bake , a the Story Girl proudly inform u when we come to the dinner-table , all on her own hook .
She be very proud of it ; and certainly as far a appearance go it justify her triumph .
The slice be smooth and golden ; and , smother in the luscious maple sugar sauce which Cecily have compound , be very fair to view .
Nevertheless , although none of u , not even Uncle Roger or Felicity , say a word at the time , for fear of hurt the Story Girl 's feeling , the pudding do not taste exactly a it should .
It be tough -- decidedly tough -- and lack the richness of flavour which be customary in Aunt Janet 's cornmeal pudding .
If it have not be for the abundant supply of sauce it would have be very dry eat indeed .
Eaten it be , however , to the last crumb .
If it be not just what a cornmeal pudding might be , the rest of the bill of fare have be extra good and our appetite match it .
`` I wish I be twin so 's I could eat more , '' say Dan , when he simply have to stop .
`` What good would be twin do you ? ''
ask Peter .
`` People who squint ca n't eat any more than people who do n't squint , can they ? ''
We could not see any connection between Peter 's two question .
`` What have squint get to do with twin ? ''
ask Dan .
`` Why , twin be just people that squint , be n't they ? ''
say Peter .
We think he be try to be funny , until we find out that he be quite in earnest .
Then we laugh until Peter get sulky .
`` I do n't care , '' he say .
`` How 's a fellow to know ?
Tommy and Adam Cowan , over at Markdale , be twin ; and they 're both cross-eyed .
So I s ` pose that be what be twin mean .
It 's all very fine for you fellows to laugh .
I never go to school half as much a you do ; and you be bring up in Toronto , too .
If you 'd work out ever since you be seven , and just get to school in the winter , there 'd be lot of thing you would n't know , either . ''
`` Never mind , Peter , '' say Cecily .
`` You know lot of thing they do n't . ''
But Peter be not to be conciliate , and take himself off in high dudgeon .
To be laugh at before Felicity -- to be laugh at BY Felicity -- be something he could not endure .
Let Cecily and the Story Girl cackle all they want to , and let those stuck-up Toronto boys grin like chessy-cats ; but when Felicity laugh at him the iron enter into Peter 's soul .
If the Story Girl laugh at Peter the mill of the god ground out his revenge for him in mid-afternoon .
Felicity , have use up all the available cooking material in the house , have to stop perforce ; and she now determine to stuff two new pincushion she have be make for her room .
We hear her rummage in the pantry a we sit on the cool , spruce-shadowed cellar door outside , where Uncle Roger be show u how to make elderberry pop-guns .
Presently she come out , frown .
`` Cecily , do you know where mother put the sawdust she empty out of that old bead pincushion of Grandmother King 's , after she have sift the needle out of it ?
I think it be in the tin box . ''
`` So it be , '' say Cecily .
`` It be n't .
There be n't a speck of sawdust in that box . ''
The Story Girl 's face wear a quite indescribable expression , compound of horror and shame .
She need not have confess .
If she have but hold her tongue the mystery of the sawdust 's disappearance might have forever remain a mystery .
She WOULD have hold her tongue , a she afterwards confide to me , if it have not be for a horrible fear which flash into her mind that possibly sawdust pudding be not healthy for people to eat -- especially if there might be needle in them -- and that if any mischief have be do in that direction it be her duty to undo it if possible at any cost of ridicule to herself .
`` Oh , Felicity , '' she say , her voice express a very anguish of humiliation , `` I -- I -- think that stuff in the box be cornmeal and use it to make the pudding . ''
Felicity and Cecily star blankly at the Story Girl .
We boys begin to laugh , but be check midway by Uncle Roger .
He be rock himself back and forth , with his hand press against his stomach .
`` Oh , '' he groan , `` I 've be wonder what these sharp pain I 've be feel ever since dinner meant .
I know now .
I must have swallow a needle -- several needle , perhaps .
I 'm do for ! ''
The poor Story Girl go very white .
`` Oh , Uncle Roger , could it be possible ?
You COULD N'T have swallow a needle without know it .
It would have stick in your tongue or teeth . ''
`` I do n't chew the pudding , '' groan Uncle Roger .
`` It be too tough -- I just swallow the chunk whole . ''
He groan and twisted and double himself up .
But he overdo it .
He be not as good an actor a the Story Girl .
Felicity look scornfully at him .
`` Uncle Roger , you be not one bit sick , '' she say deliberately .
`` You be just put on . ''
`` Felicity , if I die from the effect of eat sawdust pudding , flavour with needle , you 'll be sorry you ever say such a thing to your poor old uncle , '' say Uncle Roger reproachfully .
`` Even if there be no needle in it , sixty-year-old sawdust ca n't be good for my tummy .
I daresay it be n't even clean . ''
`` Well , you know every one have to eat a peck of dirt in his life , '' giggle Felicity .
`` But nobody have to eat it all at once , '' retort Uncle Roger , with another groan .
`` Oh , Sara Stanley , it 's a thankful man I be that your Aunt Olivia be to be home to-night .
You 'd have me kilt entirely by another day .
I believe you do it on purpose to have a story to tell . ''
Uncle Roger hobble off to the barn , still hold on to his stomach .
`` Do you think he really feel sick ? ''
ask the Story Girl anxiously .
`` No , I do n't , '' say Felicity .
`` You need n't worry over him .
There 's nothing the matter with him .
I do n't believe there be any needle in that sawdust .
Mother sift it very carefully . ''
`` I know a story about a man whose son swallow a mouse , '' say the Story Girl , who would probably have know a story and try to tell it if she be be lead to the stake .
`` And he run and waken up a very tired doctor just a he have get to sleep . ''
` Oh , doctor , my son have swallow a mouse , ' he cry .
` What shall I do ? ' ''
` Tell him to swallow a cat , ' roar the poor doctor , and slam his door .
`` Now , if Uncle Roger have swallow any needle , maybe it would make it all right if he swallow a pincushion . ''
We all laugh .
But Felicity soon grow sober .
`` It seem awful to think of eat a sawdust pudding .
How on earth do you make such a mistake ? ''
`` It look just like cornmeal , '' say the Story Girl , go from white to red in her shame .
`` Well , I 'm go to give up try to cook , and stick to thing I can do .
And if ever one of you mention sawdust pudding to me I 'll never tell you another story as long a I live . ''
The threat be effectual .
Never do we mention that unholy pudding .
But the Story Girl could not so impose silence on the grown-ups , especially Uncle Roger .
He torment her for the rest of the summer .
Never a breakfast do he sit down to , without gravely inquire if they be sure there be no sawdust in the porridge .
Not a tweak of rheumatism do he feel but he vow it be due to a needle , travel about his body .
And Aunt Olivia be warn to label all the pincushion in the house .
`` Contents , sawdust ; not intend for pudding . ''
CHAPTER XVIII .
HOW KISSING WAS DISCOVERED An August evening , calm , golden , dewless , can be very lovely .
At sunset , Felicity , Cecily , and Sara Ray , Dan , Felix , and I be in the orchard , sit on the cool grass at the base of the Pulpit Stone .
In the west be a field of crocus sky over which pale cloud blossom be scatter .
Uncle Roger have go to the station to meet the traveller , and the dining-room table be spread with a feast of fat thing .
`` It 's be a jolly week , take it all round , '' say Felix , `` but I 'm glad the grown-ups be come back to-night , especially Uncle Alec . ''
`` I wonder if they 'll bring u anything , '' say Dan .
`` I 'm think long to hear all about the wedding , '' say Felicity , who be braid timothy stalk into a collar for Pat .
`` You girl be always think about wedding and get marry , '' say Dan contemptuously .
`` We ai n't , '' say Felicity indignantly .
`` I be NEVER go to get marry .
I think it be just horrid , so there ! ''
`` I guess you think it would be a good deal horrider not to be , '' say Dan .
`` It depend on who you 're marry to , '' say Cecily gravely , see that Felicity disdain reply .
`` If you get a man like father it would be all right .
But S'POSEN you get one like Andrew Ward ?
He 's so mean and cross to his wife that she tell him every day she wish she 'd never set eye on him . ''
`` Perhaps that 's WHY he 's mean and cross , '' say Felix .
`` I tell you it be n't always the man 's fault , '' say Dan darkly .
`` When I get married I 'll be good to my wife , but I mean to be bos .
When I open my mouth my word will be law . ''
`` If your word be as big a your mouth I guess it will be , '' say Felicity cruelly .
`` I pity the man who get you , Felicity King , that 's all '' retort Dan .
`` Now , do n't fight , '' implore Cecily .
`` Who 's fight ? ''
demand Dan .
`` Felicity think she can say anything she like to me , but I 'll show her different . ''
Probably , in spite of Cecily 's effort , a bitter spat would have result between Dan and Felicity , have not a diversion be effect at that moment by the Story Girl , who come slowly down Uncle Stephen 's Walk .
`` Just look how the Story Girl have get herself up ! ''
say Felicity .
`` Why , she 's no more than decent ! ''
The Story Girl be barefooted and barearmed , have roll the sleeve of her pink gingham up to her shoulder .
Around her waist be twist a girdle of the blood-red rose that bloom in Aunt Olivia 's garden ; on her sleek curl she wear a chaplet of them ; and her hand be full of them .
She pause under the outmost tree , in a golden-green gloom , and laugh at u over a big branch .
Her wild , subtle , nameless charm clothe her a with a garment .
We always remember the picture she make there ; and in late day when we read Tennyson 's poem at a college desk , we know exactly how an oread , peer through the green leaf on some haunt knoll of many fountained Ida , must look .
`` Felicity , '' say the Story Girl reproachfully , `` what have you be do to Peter ?
He 's up there sulk in the granary , and he wo n't come down , and he say it 's your fault .
You must have hurt his feeling dreadfully . ''
`` I do n't know about his feeling , '' say Felicity , with an angry toss of her shin head , `` but I guess I make his ear tingle all right .
I box them both good and hard . ''
`` Oh , Felicity !
What for ? ''
`` Well , he try to kiss me , that 's what for ! ''
say Felicity , turn very red .
`` As if I would let a hired boy kiss me !
I guess Master Peter wo n't try anything like that again in a hurry . ''
The Story Girl come out of her shadow and sit down beside u on the grass .
`` Well , in that case , '' she say gravely , `` I think you do right to slap his ear -- not because he be a hired boy , but because it would be impertinent in ANY boy .
But talk of kiss make me think of a story I find in Aunt Olivia 's scrapbook the other day .
Would n't you like to hear it ?
It be call , ` How Kissing Was Discovered . ' ''
`` Was n't kiss always discover ? ''
ask Dan .
`` Not accord to this story .
It be just discover accidentally . ''
`` Well , let 's hear about it , '' say Felix , `` although I think kiss 's awful silly , and it would n't have matter much if it have n't ever be discover . ''
The Story Girl scatter her rose around her on the grass , and clasp her slim hand over her knee .
Gazing dreamily afar at the tinted sky between the apple tree , a if she be look back to the merry day of the world 's gay youth , she begin , her voice give to the word and fancy of the old tale the delicacy of hoar frost and the crystal sparkle of dew .
`` It happen long , long ago in Greece -- where so many other beautiful thing happen .
Before that , nobody have ever hear of kissing .
And then it be just discover in the twinkling of an eye .
And a man write it down and the account have be preserve ever since .
`` There be a young shepherd name Glaucon -- a very handsome young shepherd -- who live in a little village call Thebes .
It become a very great and famous city afterwards , but at this time it be only a little village , very quiet and simple .
Too quiet for Glaucon 's liking .
He grow tire of it , and he think he would like to go away from home and see something of the world .
So he take his knapsack and his shepherd 's crook , and wander away until he come to Thessaly .
That be the land of the god ' hill , you know .
The name of the hill be Olympus .
But it have nothing to do with this story .
This happen on another mountain -- Mount Pelion .
`` Glaucon hire himself to a wealthy man who have a great many sheep .
And every day Glaucon have to lead the sheep up to pasture on Mount Pelion , and watch them while they eat .
There be nothing else to do , and he would have find the time very long , if he have not be able to play on a flute .
So he play very often and very beautifully , a he sit under the tree and watch the wonderful blue sea afar off , and think about Aglaia .
`` Aglaia be his master 's daughter .
She be so sweet and beautiful that Glaucon fell in love with her the very moment he first saw her ; and when he be not play his flute on the mountain he be think about Aglaia , and dream that some day he might have flock of his own , and a dear little cottage down in the valley where he and Aglaia might live .
`` Aglaia have fall in love with Glaucon just a he have with her .
But she never let him suspect it for ever so long .
He do not know how often she would steal up the mountain and hide behind the rock near where the sheep pasture , to listen to Glaucon 's beautiful music .
It be very lovely music , because he be always think of Aglaia while he play , though he little dream how near him she often be .
`` But after awhile Glaucon find out that Aglaia love him , and everything be well .
Nowadays I suppose a wealthy man like Aglaia 's father would n't be willing to let his daughter marry a hired man ; but this be in the Golden Age , you know , when nothing like that matter at all .
`` After that , almost every day Aglaia would go up the mountain and sit beside Glaucon , a he watch the flock and play on his flute .
But he do not play as much a he use to , because he like well to talk with Aglaia .
And in the evening they would lead the sheep home together .
`` One day Aglaia go up the mountain by a new way , and she come to a little brook .
Something be sparkle very brightly among it pebble .
Aglaia pick it up , and it be the most beautiful little stone that she have ever see .
It be only as large a a pea , but it glitter and flash in the sunlight with every colour of the rainbow .
Aglaia be so delighted with it that she resolve to take it a a present to Glaucon .
`` But all at once she hear a stamping of hoof behind her , and when she turn she almost die from fright .
For there be the great god , Pan , and he be a very terrible object , look quite as much like a goat a a man .
The god be not all beautiful , you know .
And , beautiful or not , nobody ever want to meet them face to face . ''
` Give that stone to me , ' say Pan , hold out his hand .
`` But Aglaia , though she be frighten , would not give him the stone . '' '
I want it for Glaucon , ' she say . '' '
I want it for one of my wood nymphs , ' say Pan , ` and I must have it . '
`` He advance threateningly , but Aglaia run as hard a she could up the mountain .
If she could only reach Glaucon he would protect her .
Pan follow her , clatter and bellow terribly , but in a few minute she rush into Glaucon 's arm .
`` The dreadful sight of Pan and the still more dreadful noise he make , so frighten the sheep that they flee in all direction .
But Glaucon be not afraid at all , because Pan be the god of shepherd , and be bind to grant any prayer a good shepherd , who always do his duty , might make .
If Glaucon have NOT be a good shepherd dear know what would have happen to him and Aglaia .
But he be ; and when he beg Pan to go away and not frighten Aglaia any more , Pan have to go , grumble a good deal -- and Pan 's grumbling have a very ugly sound .
But still he WENT , and that be the main thing . ''
` Now , dear , what be all this trouble about ? '
ask Glaucon ; and Aglaia tell him the story . ''
` But where be the beautiful stone ? '
he ask , when she have finish .
` Didst thou drop it in thy alarm ? '
`` No , indeed !
Aglaia have do nothing of the sort .
When she begin to run , she have pop it into her mouth , and there it be still , quite safe .
Now she poke it out between her red lip , where it glitter in the sunlight . ''
` Take it , ' she whisper .
`` The question be -- how be he to take it ?
Both of Aglaia 's arm be hold fast to her side by Glaucon 's arm ; and if he loosen his clasp ever so little he be afraid she would fall , so weak and trembling be she from her dreadful fright .
Then Glaucon have a brilliant idea .
He would take the beautiful stone from Aglaia 's lip with his own lip .
`` He bend over until his lip touch hers -- and THEN , he forget all about the beautiful pebble and so do Aglaia .
Kissing be discover !
`` What a yarn ! ''
say Dan , draw a long breath , when we have come to ourselves and discover that we be really sit in a dewy Prince Edward Island orchard instead of watch two lover on a mountain in Thessaly in the Golden Age .
`` I do n't believe a word of it . ''
`` Of course , we know it be n't really true , '' say Felicity .
`` Well , I do n't know , '' say the Story Girl thoughtfully .
`` I think there be two kind of true thing -- true thing that ARE , and true thing that be NOT , but MIGHT be . ''
`` I do n't believe there 's any but the one kind of trueness , '' say Felicity .
`` And anyway , this story could n't be true .
You know there be no such thing a a god Pan . ''
`` How do you know what there might have be in the Golden Age ? ''
ask the Story Girl .
Which be , indeed , an unanswerable question for Felicity .
`` I wonder what become of the beautiful stone ? ''
say Cecily .
`` Likely Aglaia swallow it , '' say Felix practically .
`` Did Glaucon and Aglaia ever get marry ? ''
ask Sara Ray .
`` The story do n't say .
It stop just there , '' say the Story Girl .
`` But of course they do .
I will tell you what I think .
I do n't think Aglaia swallow the stone .
I think it just fell to the ground ; and after awhile they find it , and it turn out to be of such value that Glaucon could buy all the flock and herd in the valley , and the sweet cottage ; and he and Aglaia be marry right away . ''
`` But you only THINK that , '' say Sara Ray .
`` I 'd like to be really sure that be what happen . ''
`` Oh , bother , none of it happen , '' say Dan .
`` I believe it while the Story Girl be tell it , but I do n't now .
Is n't that wheel ? ''
Wheels it be .
Two wagon be drive up the lane .
We rush to the house -- and there be Uncle Alec and Aunt Janet and Aunt Olivia !
The excitement be quite tremendous .
Every body talk and laugh at once , and it be not until we be all seat around the supper table that conversation grow coherent .
What laughter and questioning and telling of tale follow , what smile and bright eye and glad voice .
And through it all , the blissful purr of Paddy , who sit on the window sill behind the Story Girl , resound through the din like Andrew McPherson 's bass -- `` just a bur-r-r-r the hale time . ''
`` Well , I 'm thankful to be home again '' say Aunt Janet , beam on u .
`` We have a real nice time , and Edward 's folk be as kind a could be .
But give me home for a steady thing .
How have everything go ?
How do the child behave , Roger ? ''
`` Like model , '' say Uncle Roger .
`` They be as good a gold most of the day . ''
There be time when one could n't help like Uncle Roger .
CHAPTER XIX .
A DREAD PROPHECY `` I 've get to go and begin stump out the elderberry pasture this afternoon , '' say Peter dolefully .
`` I tell you it 's a tough job .
Mr. Roger might wait for cool weather before he set people to stump out elderberry , and that 's a fact . ''
`` Why do n't you tell him so ? ''
ask Dan .
`` It ai n't my business to tell him thing , '' retort Peter .
`` I 'm hired to do what I 'm told , and I do it .
But I can have my own opinion all the same .
It 's go to be a broiling hot day . ''
We be all in the orchard , except Felix , who have go to the post-office .
It be the forenoon of an August Saturday .
Cecily and Sara Ray , who have come up to spend the day with u -- her mother have go to town -- be eat timothy root .
Bertha Lawrence , a Charlottetown girl , who have visit Kitty Marr in June , and have go to school one day with her , have eat timothy root , affect to consider them great delicacy .
The fad be at once take up by the Carlisle schoolgirl .
Timothy root quite oust `` sour '' and young raspberry sprout , both of which have the real merit of be quite toothsome , while timothy root be tough and tasteless .
But timothy root be fashionable , therefore timothy root must be eat .
Pecks of them must have be devour in Carlisle that summer .
Pat be there also , pad about from one to the other on his black paw , give u friendly poke and rub .
We all make much of him except Felicity , who would not take any notice of him because he be the Story Girl 's cat .
We boy be sprawl on the grass .
Our morning chore be do and the day be before u .
We should have be feel very comfortable and happy , but , a a matter of fact , we be not particularly so .
The Story Girl be sit on the mint beside the well-house , weave herself a wreath of buttercup .
Felicity be sip from the cup of clouded blue with an overdone air of unconcern .
Each be acutely and miserably conscious of the other 's presence , and each be desirous of convince the rest of u that the other be less than nothing to her .
Felicity could not succeed .
The Story Girl manage it well .
If it have not be for the fact that in all our foregatherings she be careful to sit a far from Felicity a possible , we might have be deceive .
We have not pass a very pleasant week .
Felicity and the Story Girl have not be `` speak '' to each other , and consequently there have be something rotten in the state of Denmark .
An air of restraint be over all our game and conversation .
On the precede Monday Felicity and the Story Girl have quarrel over something .
What the cause of the quarrel be I can not tell because I never know .
It remain a `` dead secret '' between the party of the first and second part forever .
But it be more bitter than the general run of their tiff , and the consequence be apparent to all .
They have not speak to each other since .
This be not because the rancour of either last so long .
On the contrary it pass speedily away , not even one low descend sun go down on their wrath .
But dignity remain to be consider .
Neither would `` speak first , '' and each obstinately declare that she would not speak first , no , not in a hundred year .
Neither argument , entreaty , nor expostulation have any effect on those two stubborn girl , nor yet the tear of sweet Cecily , who cry every night about it , and mingle in her pure little prayer fervent petition that Felicity and the Story Girl might make up .
`` I do n't know where you expect to go when you die , Felicity , '' she say tearfully , `` if you do n't forgive people . ''
`` I have forgive her , '' be Felicity 's answer , `` but I be not go to speak first for all that . ''
`` It 's very wrong , and , more than that , it 's so uncomfortable , '' complain Cecily .
`` It spoil everything . ''
`` Were they ever like this before ? ''
I ask Cecily , a we talk the matter over privately in Uncle Stephen 's Walk .
`` Never for so long , '' say Cecily .
`` They have a spell like this last summer , and one the summer before , but they only last a couple of day . ''
`` And who speak first ? ''
`` Oh , the Story Girl .
She get excite about something and speak to Felicity before she think , and then it be all right .
But I 'm afraid it be n't go to be like that this time .
Do n't you notice how careful the Story Girl be not to get excite ?
That be such a bad sign . ''
`` We 've just get to think up something that will excite her , that 's all , '' I say .
`` I 'm -- I 'm pray about it , '' say Cecily in a low voice , her tear-wet lash tremble against her pale , round cheek .
`` Do you suppose it will do any good , Bev ? ''
`` Very likely , '' I assure her .
`` Remember Sara Ray and the money .
That come from pray . ''
`` I 'm glad you think so , '' say Cecily tremulously .
`` Dan say it be no use for me to bother pray about it .
He say if they COULD N'T speak God might do something , but when they just WOULD N'T it be n't likely He would interfere .
Dan do say such queer thing .
I 'm so afraid he 's go to grow up just like Uncle Robert Ward , who never go to church , and do n't believe more than half the Bible be true . ''
`` Which half do he believe be true ? ''
I inquire with unholy curiosity .
`` Oh , just the nice part .
He say there 's a heaven all right , but no -- no -- HELL .
I do n't want Dan to grow up like that .
It be n't respectable .
And you would n't want all kind of people crowd heaven , now , would you ? ''
`` Well , no , I suppose not , '' I agree , think of Billy Robinson .
`` Of course , I ca n't help feeling sorry for those who have to go to THE OTHER PLACE , '' say Cecily compassionately .
`` But I suppose they would n't be very comfortable in heaven either .
They would n't feel at home .
Andrew Marr say a simply dreadful thing about THE OTHER PLACE one night last fall , when Felicity and I be down to see Kitty , and they be burn the potato stalk .
He say he believe THE OTHER PLACE must be lot more interesting than heaven because fire be such jolly thing .
Now , do you ever hear the like ? ''

CHAPTER XX .
THE JUDGMENT SUNDAY Sunday morning break , dull and gray .

Ay , doubtless .
That dauntless spirit would soar triumphantly above the wreck of matter and the crash of world , take with it all it own wild sweetness and daring .

Some vague thought of this be in our mind a we look at her ; and somehow it comfort u .

`` It must be get handy two , '' say Cecily .

Would two o'clock never come and end the suspense ?
We all become very tense .
Even Peter have to stop reading .
Any unaccustomed sound or sight in the world about u strike on our taut sens like the trump of doom .

But oh , I wish that clock would strike two . ''

I entreat the Story Girl .
She shake her head .
`` No , it would be no use to try .
But if this be n't the Judgment Day I 'll have a great one to tell of u be so scar . ''
Pat presently come gallop up the orchard , carry in his mouth a big field mouse , which , sit down before u , he proceed to devour , body and bone , afterwards lick his chop with great satisfaction .

We watch her white-clad figure pas through the gate and enter the front door .

Then Cecily come run at full speed back to u .
But when she reach u she tremble so much that at first she could not speak .
`` What be it ?
Is it past two ? ''
implore the Story Girl .

say Felix , a we walk down the hill .

`` Tell u it now . ''

`` Long ago , when Judy Pineau be young , '' say the Story Girl , `` she be hire with Mrs. Elder Frewen -- the first Mrs. Elder Frewen .

CHAPTER XXI .
DREAMERS OF DREAMS August go out and September come in .
Harvest be end ; and though summer be not yet go , her face be turn westering .
The aster letter her retreat footstep in a purple script , and over the hill and valley hang a faint blue smoke , a if Nature be worship at her woodland altar .
The apple begin to burn red on the bending bough ; cricket sing day and night ; squirrel chatter secret of Polichinelle in the spruce ; the sunshine be a thick and yellow a molten gold ; school open , and we small denizen of the hill farm live happy day of harmless work and necessary play , close in night of peaceful , undisturbed slumber under a roof watch over by autumnal star .
At least , our slumber be peaceful and undisturbed until our orgy of dream begin .
`` I would really like to know what especial kind of deviltry you young fry be up to this time , '' say Uncle Roger one evening , a he pass through the orchard with his gun on his shoulder , bound for the swamp .
We be sit in a circle before the Pulpit Stone , each write diligently in an exercise book , and eat the Rev . Mr. Scott 's plum , which always reach their prime of juicy , golden-green flesh and bloomy blue skin in September .
The Rev . Mr. Scott be dead and go , but those plum certainly keep his memory green , a his forgotten sermon could never have do .
`` Oh , '' say Felicity in a shocked tone , when Uncle Roger have pass by , `` Uncle Roger SWORE . ''

` Deviltry ' be n't swear at all .
It only mean extra bad mischief . ''
`` Well , it 's not a very nice word , anyhow , '' say Felicity .
`` No , it be n't , '' agree the Story Girl with a regretful sigh .
`` It 's very expressive , but it be n't nice .
That be the way with so many word .
They 're expressive , but they 're not nice , and so a girl ca n't use them '' The Story Girl sigh again .
She love expressive word , and treasure them a some girl might have treasure jewel .
To her , they be as lustrous pearl , thread on the crimson cord of a vivid fancy .
When she meet with a new one she utter it over and over to herself in solitude , weigh it , caress it , infuse it with the radiance of her voice , make it her own in all it possibility for ever .
`` Well , anyhow , it be n't a suitable word in this case , '' insist Felicity .
`` We be not up to any dev -- any extra bad mischief .
Writing down one 's dream be n't mischief at all . ''
Certainly it be n't .
Surely not even the strait sect of the grown-ups could call it so .
If write down your dream , with agonize care a to composition and spelling -- for who know that the eye of generation unborn might not read the record ?
-- be not a harmless amusement , could anything be call so ?
I trow not .
We have be at it for a fortnight , and during that time we only live to have dream and write them down .
The Story Girl have originate the idea one evening in the rustling , rain-wet way of the spruce wood , where we be pick gum after a day of shower .
When we have pick enough , we sit down on the moss-grown stone at the end of a long arcade , where it open out on the harvest-golden valley below u , our jaw exercise themselves vigorously on the spoil of our climbing .
We be never allow to chew gum in school or in company , but in wood and field , orchard and hayloft , such rule be in abeyance .
`` My Aunt Jane use to say it be n't polite to chew gum anywhere , '' say Peter rather ruefully .
`` I do n't suppose your Aunt Jane know all the rule of etiquette , '' say Felicity , design to crush Peter with a big word , borrow from the Family Guide .
But Peter be not to be so crushed .
He have in him a certain toughness of fibre , that would have be proof against a whole dictionary .
`` She do , too , '' he retort .
`` My Aunt Jane be a real lady , even if she be only a Craig .
She know all those rule and she keep them when there be nobody round to see her , just the same a when any one be .
And she be smart .
If father have have half her git-up-and-git I would n't be a hired boy to-day . ''
`` Have you any idea where your father be ? ''
ask Dan .
`` No , '' say Peter indifferently .
`` The last we hear of him he be in the Maine lumber wood .
But that be three year ago .
I do n't know where he be now , and , '' add Peter deliberately , take his gum from his mouth to make his statement more impressive , `` I do n't care . ''
`` Oh , Peter , that sound dreadful , '' say Cecily .
`` Your own father ! ''
`` Well , '' say Peter defiantly , `` if your own father have run away when you be a baby , and leave your mother to earn her living by wash and work out , I guess you would n't care much about him either . ''
`` Perhaps your father may come home some of these day with a huge fortune , '' suggest the Story Girl .
`` Perhaps pig may whistle , but they 've poor mouth for it , '' be all the answer Peter deign to this charming suggestion .
`` There go Mr. Campbell down the road , '' say Dan .
`` That 's his new mare .
Is n't she a dandy ?
She 's get a skin like black satin .
He call her Betty Sherman . ''
`` I do n't think it 's very nice to call a horse after your own grandmother , '' say Felicity .
`` Betty Sherman would have think it a compliment , '' say the Story Girl .
`` Maybe she would .
She could n't have be very nice herself , or she would never have go and ask a man to marry her , '' say Felicity .
`` Why not ? ''

Would YOU do such a thing yourself ? ''

`` If I want him DREADFULLY , and HE would n't do the asking , perhaps I would . ''

`` Nobody as pretty a you will ever be an old maid , Felicity , '' say Peter , who never put too fine an edge on his compliment .
Felicity toss her golden tressed head and try to look angry , but make a dismal failure of it .

The Story Girl never hold the Family Guide in such reverence a do Felicity and Cecily .
They pore over the `` etiquette column '' every week , and could have tell you on demand , just exactly what kind of glove should be wear at a wedding , what you should say when introduce or be introduce , and how you ought to look when your best young man come to see you .

She be one of those woman who be always say ' I tell you so -- ' '' `` Take notice , Felicity , '' say Dan aside . ''
-- And she be very stubborn .

He say it be a Fameuse and she declare it be a Yellow Transparent .
They fight over it till the neighbour come out to listen .
Finally he get so angry that he tell her to shut up .
They do n't have any Family Guide in those day , so he do n't know it be n't polite to say shut up to your wife .
I suppose she think she would teach him manner , for would you believe it ?
That woman do shut up , and never speak one single word to her husband for five year .

And then she speak at last .
She say , ' I tell you so . ' ''

ask Sara Ray .

It stop when she speak at last .
You 're never satisfy to leave a story where it should stop , Sara Ray . ''
`` Well , I always like to know what happen afterwards , '' say Sara Ray .

`` He say it would be too tame a life for him . ''

say Cecily .
`` I 've never see any one marry , and I 'd just love to .
I 've be to four funeral , but not to one single wedding . ''
`` I 've never even get to a funeral , '' say Sara Ray gloomily .
`` There 's the wedding veil of the proud princess , '' say Cecily , point to a long drift of filmy vapour in the southwestern sky .
`` And look at that sweet pink cloud below it , '' add Felicity .
`` Maybe that little pink cloud be a dream , get all ready to float down into somebody 's sleep , '' suggest the Story Girl .
`` I have a perfectly awful dream last night , '' say Cecily , with a shudder of remembrance .
`` I dream I be on a desert island inhabit by tiger and native with two head . ''
`` Oh ! ''
the Story Girl look at Cecily half reproachfully .

If I have such a dream I could tell it so that everybody else would feel a if they have dream it , too . ''
`` Well , I 'm not you , '' counter Cecily , `` and I would n't want to frighten any one a I be frighten .
It be an awful dream -- but it be kind of interesting , too . ''
`` I 've have some real int ` rest dream , '' say Peter , `` but I ca n't remember them long .
I wish I could . ''
`` Why do n't you write them down ? ''
suggest the Story Girl .
`` Oh -- '' she turn upon u a face illuminate with a sudden inspiration .
`` I 've an idea .
Let u each get an exercise book and write down all our dream , just a we dream them .
We 'll see who 'll have the most interesting collection .
And we 'll have them to read and laugh over when we 're old and gray . ''
Instantly we all saw ourselves and each other by inner vision , old and gray -- all but the Story Girl .
We could not picture her a old .
Always , as long a she live , so it seem to u , must she have sleek brown curl , a voice like the sound of a harpstring in the wind , and eye that be star of eternal youth .
CHAPTER XXII .
THE DREAM BOOKS The next day the Story Girl coax Uncle Roger to take her to Markdale , and there she buy our dream book .
They be ten cent apiece , with rule page and mottle green cover .
My own lie open beside me a I write , it yellow page inscribe with the vision that haunt my childish slumber on those night of long ago .
On the cover be paste a lady 's visit card , on which be write , `` The Dream Book of Beverley King . ''
Cecily have a packet of visit card which she be hoard against the day when she would be grow up and could put the call etiquette of the Family Guide into practice ; but she generously give u all one apiece for the cover of our dream book .
As I turn the page and glance over the na & iuml ; ve record , each one beginning , `` Last night I dream , '' the past come very vividly back to me .
I see that bowery orchard , shin in memory with a soft glow of beauty -- `` the light that never be on land or sea , '' -- where we sit on those September evening and write down our dream , when the care of the day be over and there be nothing to interfere with the pleasing throe of composition .
Peter -- Dan -- Felix -- Cecily -- Felicity -- Sara Ray -- the Story Girl -- they be all around me once more , in the sweet-scented , fading grass , each with open dream book and pencil in hand , now write busily , now star fixedly into space in search of some elusive word or phrase which might best describe the indescribable .
I hear their laughing voice , I see their bright , unclouded eye .
In this little , old book , fill with cramped , boyish writing , there be a spell of white magic that set the year at naught .
Beverley King be a boy once more , write down his dream in the old King orchard on the homestead hill , blow over by musky wind .
Opposite to him sit the Story Girl , with her scarlet rosetted head , her beautiful bare foot cross before her , one slender hand prop her high , white brow , on either side of which fall her glossy curl .
There , to the right , be sweet Cecily of the dear , brown eye , with a little bloated dictionary beside her -- for you dream of so many thing you ca n't spell , or be expect to spell , when you be only eleven .
Next to her sits Felicity , beautiful , and conscious that she be beautiful , with hair of spun sunshine , and sea-blue eye , and all the rose of that vanish summer abloom in her cheek .
Peter be beside her , of course , sprawl flat on his stomach among the grass , one hand clutch his black curl , with his dream book on a small , round stone before him -- for only so can Peter compose at all , and even then he find it hard work .
He can handle a hoe more deftly than a pencil , and his spelling , even with all his frequent appeal to Cecily , be a fearful and wonderful thing .
As for punctuation , he never attempt it , beyond an occasion period , jot down whenever he happen to think of it , whether in the right place or not .
The Story Girl go over his dream after he have write them out , and put in the comma and semicolon , and straighten out the sentence .
Felix sit on the right of the Story Girl , fat and stodgy , grimly in earnest even over dream .
He write with his knee stick up to form a writing-desk , and he always frowns fiercely the whole time .
Dan , like Peter , write lie down flat , but with his back towards u ; and he have a dismal habit of groan aloud , writhe his whole body , and dig his toe into the grass , when he can not turn a sentence to suit him .
Sara Ray be at his left .
There be seldom anything to be say of Sara except to tell where she be .
Like Tennyson 's Maud , in one respect at least , Sara be splendidly null .
Well , there we sit and write in our dream book , and Uncle Roger pass by and accuses u of be up to dev -- to very bad mischief .
Each of u be very anxious to possess the most exciting record ; but we be an honourable little crew , and I do not think anything be ever write down in those dream book which have not really be dream .
We have expect that the Story Girl would eclipse u all in the matter of dream ; but , at least in the beginning , her dream be no more remarkable than those of the rest of u .
In dreamland we be all equal .
Cecily , indeed , seem to have the most decided talent for dramatic dream .
That meek and mild of girl be in the habit of dream truly terrible thing .
Almost every night battle , murder , or sudden death play some part in her vision .
On the other hand , Dan , who be a somewhat truculent fellow , addict to the perusal of lurid dime novel which he borrow from the other boy in school , dream dream of such a peaceful and pastoral character that he be quite disgust with the result tame page of his dream book .
But if the Story Girl could not dream anything more wonderful than the rest of u , she score when it come to the telling .
To hear her tell a dream be as good -- or a bad -- a dream it yourself .
As far a write them down be concerned , I believe that I , Beverley King , carry off the palm .
I be consider to possess a pretty knack of composition .
But the Story Girl go me one good even there , because , have inherit something of her father 's talent for drawing , she illustrate her dream with sketch that certainly catch the spirit of them , whatever might be say of their technical excellence .
She have an especial knack for draw monstrosity ; and I vividly recall the picture of an enormous and hideous lizard , look like a reptile of the pterodactyl period , which she have dream of see crawl across the roof of the house .
On another occasion she have a frightful dream -- at least , it seem frightful while she tell u and describe the dreadful feeling it have give her -- of be chase around the parlour by the ottoman , which make face at her .
She draw a picture of the grimace ottoman on the margin of her dream book which so scar Sara Ray when she behold it that she cry all the way home , and insist on sleep that night with Judy Pineau l the furniture take to pursue her also .
Sara Ray 's own dream never amount to much .
She be always in trouble of some sort -- could n't get her hair braid , or her shoe on the right foot .
Consequently , her dream book be very monotonous .
The only thing worth mention in the way of dream that Sara Ray ever achieve be when she dream that she go up in a balloon and fell out .
`` I expect to come down with an awful thud , '' she say shuddering , `` but I light as light a a feather and wake right up . ''
`` If you have n't wake up you 'd have die , '' say Peter with a dark significance .
`` If you dream of fall and DO N'T wake you DO land with a thud and it kill you .
That 's what happen to people who die in their sleep . ''
`` How do you know ? ''
ask Dan skeptically .
`` Nobody who die in his sleep could ever tell it . ''
`` My Aunt Jane tell me so , '' say Peter .
`` I suppose that settle it , '' say Felicity disagreeably .
`` You always say something nasty when I mention my Aunt Jane , '' say Peter reproachfully .
`` What do I say that be nasty ? ''
cry Felicity .
`` I do n't say a single thing . ''
`` Well , it sound nasty , '' say Peter , who know that it be the tone that make the music .
`` What do your Aunt Jane look like ? ''
ask Cecily sympathetically .
`` Was she pretty ? ''
`` No , '' concede Peter reluctantly , `` she be n't pretty -- but she look like the woman in that picture the Story Girl 's father send her last week -- the one with the shiny ring round her head and the baby in her lap .
I 've see Aunt Jane look at me just like that woman look at her baby .
Ma never look so .
Poor ma be too busy wash .
I wish I could dream of my Aunt Jane .
I never do . '' ''
` Dream of the dead , you 'll hear of the living , ' '' quote Felix oracularly .
`` I dream last night that I throw a lighted match into that keg of gunpowder in Mr. Cook 's store at Markdale , '' say Peter .
`` It blow up -- and everything blow up -- and they fish me out of the mess -- but I wake up before I 'd time to find out if I be kill or not . ''

`` And oh , I be so happy !
It be dreadful to wake up and find it as straight a ever . ''
Felix , that sober , solid fellow , dream constantly of fly through the air .
His description of his aerial flight over the tree-tops of dreamland always fill u with envy .
None of the rest of u could ever compass such a dream , not even the Story Girl , who might have be expect to dream of fly if anybody do .
Felix have a knack of dream anyhow , and his dream book , while suffer somewhat in comparison of literary style , be about the best of the lot when it come to subject matter .
Cecily 's might be more dramatic , but Felix 's be more amusing .
The dream which we all count his masterpiece be the one in which a menagerie have camp in the orchard and the rhinoceros chase Aunt Janet around and around the Pulpit Stone , but turn into an inoffensive pig when it be on the point of catch her .

But Felix flatly refuse to take liver pill ; Mexican Tea he would drink , but liver pill he would not take , in spite of his own suffering and Aunt Janet 's command and entreaty .
I could not understand his antipathy to the insignificant little white pellet , which be so easy to swallow ; but he explain the matter to u in the orchard when he have recover his usual health and spirit .
`` I be afraid to take the liver pill for fear they 'd prevent me from dream , '' he say .
`` Do n't you remember old Miss Baxter in Toronto , Bev ?
And how she tell Mrs. McLaren that she be subject to terrible dream , and finally she take two liver pill and never have any more dream after that .
I 'd rather have die than risk it , '' conclude Felix solemnly .
`` I 'd an exciting dream last night for once , '' say Dan triumphantly .
`` I dream old Peg Bowen chase me .
I think I be up to her house and she take after me .
You bet I scoot .
And she catch me -- yes , sir !
I felt her skinny hand reach out and clutch my shoulder .
I let out a screech -- and wake up . ''
`` I should think you do screech , '' say Felicity .
`` We hear you clean over into our room . ''

`` I just stand root to the ground -- and see it come -- and ca n't stir .
It do n't sound much write out , but it 's awful to go through .

`` I wonder what Peg Bowen would really do to a fellow if she catch him , '' speculate Dan .
`` Peg Bowen do n't need to catch you to do thing to you , '' say Peter ominously .
`` She can put ill-luck on you just by look at you -- and she will if you offend her . ''
`` I do n't believe that , '' say the Story Girl airily .
`` Do n't you ?
All right , then !
Last summer she call at Lem Hill 's in Markdale , and he tell her to clear out or he 'd set the dog on her .
Peg clear out , and she go across his pasture , mutter to herself and throw her arm round .
And next day his very best cow take sick and die .
How do you account for that ? ''
`` It might have happen anyhow , '' say the Story Girl -- somewhat less assuredly , though .
`` It might .
But I 'd just as soon Peg Bowen do n't look at MY cow , '' say Peter .
`` As if you have any cow ! ''
giggle Felicity .
`` I 'm go to have cow some day , '' say Peter , flushing .
`` I do n't mean to be a hired boy all my life .

`` I dream last night that we open the blue chest , '' say the Story Girl , `` and all the thing be there -- the blue china candlestick -- only it be brass in the dream -- and the fruit basket with the apple on it , and the wedding dress , and the embroidered petticoat .
And we be laugh , and try the thing on , and have such fun .

`` I dream last night that Felix be thin , '' say Peter , laugh .
`` He do look so queer .
His clothes just hang loose , and he be go round try to hold them on . ''
Everybody think this be funny , except Felix .
He would not speak to Peter for two day because of it .
Felicity also get into trouble because of her dream .
One night she wake up , have just have a very exciting dream ; but she go to sleep again , and in the morning she could not remember the dream at all .
Felicity determine she would never let another dream get away from her in such a fashion ; and the next time she waken in the night -- have dream that she be dead and bury -- she promptly arise , light a candle , and proceed to write the dream down then and there .
While so employed she contrive to upset the candle and set fire to her nightgown -- a brand-new one , trim with any quantity of crocheted lace .
A huge hole be burn in it , and when Aunt Janet discover it she lift up her voice with no uncertain sound .
Felicity have never receive a sharp scolding .
But she take it very philosophically .
She be use to her mother 's bitter tongue , and she be not unduly sensitive .
`` Anyhow , I save my dream , '' she say placidly .
And that , of course , be all that really matter .
Grown people be so strangely oblivious to the truly important thing of life .
Material for new garment , of night or day , could be buy in any shop for a trifling sum and make up out of hand .
But if a dream escape you , in what market-place the wide world over can you hope to regain it ?
What coin of earthly minting will ever buy back for you that lose and lovely vision ?
CHAPTER XXIII .
SUCH STUFF AS DREAMS ARE MADE ON Peter take Dan and me aside one evening , a we be on our way to the orchard with our dream book , say significantly that he want our advice .
Accordingly , we go round to the spruce wood , where the girl would not see u to the rousing of their curiosity , and then Peter tell u of his dilemma .
`` Last night I dream I be in church , '' he say .
`` I think it be full of people , and I walk up the aisle to your pew and set down , as unconcerned a a pig on ice .
And then I find that I have n't a stitch of clothes on -- NOT ONE BLESSED STITCH .
Now '' -- Peter drop his voice -- `` what be bother me be this -- would it be proper to tell a dream like that before the girl ? ''
I be of the opinion that it would be rather questionable ; but Dan vow he do n't see why .
HE 'D tell it quick a any other dream .
There be nothing bad in it .
`` But they 're your own relation , '' say Peter .
`` They 're no relation to me , and that make a difference .
Besides , they 're all such ladylike girl .
I guess I 'd well not risk it .
I 'm pretty sure Aunt Jane would n't think it be proper to tell such a dream .
And I do n't want to offend Fel -- any of them . ''
